When Does Citing God's Will Become Blameworthy?
The objection from three Quranic verses and the first part of the answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God blamed the polytheists for saying 'If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners' and how they misused divine will as evidence of His approval.

Core Idea
Citing God's will is only true when not used to escape responsibility.

The polytheists used a seemingly pious phrase—'If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners'—to excuse their shirk. Yet God severely criticized them for it. This lesson unpacks the first layer of the classical answer: God denounced them because they interpreted His will as a sign of His pleasure, as if whatever He wills must be pleasing to Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses of the polytheists' argument
Read the three Quranic verses where polytheists invoke God's will as a defense.
Notice how they use 'if Allah had willed' to claim inevitability.
2
Understand the objection
The objection is that these verses seem to excuse polytheism if God willed it.
3
Examine the answer
The answer says they were blamed for using His will as proof of His approval, implying that whatever He wills He loves.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Reflect on how divine will (mashī'a) does not necessarily equal divine pleasure (ridā).

فإن قيل: يشكل على هذا قوله تعالى: سَيَقُولُ الَّذِينَ اشْرَكُوا لَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا أَشْرَكْنَا وَ لَا آبَاؤُنَا وَلَا حَرَّمْنَا مِن شَى الآية [الأنعام: ١٤٨]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَالَ الَّذِينَ اشْرَ كَوْا لَوْ شَاء اللَّهُ مَا عَبَدَنَا مِنْ دُونِهِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ نَحْنُ وَلَا أَبَا وَنَا وَ لَا حَرَّ مُنَا مِنْ دُونِهِ مِنْ شَيْ﴾ الآية [النحل : ٣٥]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَوْشَاء الرَّحْمٰنُ مَا عَبَدُ ذَهُمْ مَا لَهُمْ بِذلِكَ مِنْ عِلْمٍ إِنْ هُمْ أَلَّا يَخْرُصُونَ ﴾ [الزخرف: ۲۰] ، أي يكذبون أو يظنون ويتوهمون فقد ذمهم الله تعالى حيث جعلوا الشرك كائنا منهم لمشيئة الله. وكذلك ذم إبليس حيث أضاف الإغواء إلى الله تعالى إذ قال : رب بما أغويتني لأزينن لهم في الأرض [ الحجر : ٣٩]. والجواب: أنه أنكر عليهم ذلك لأنهم احتجوا بمشيئته على رضاه ومحبته وقالوا: لو كره ذلك وسخط لما شاء، فجعلوا مشيئة الله دليل رضاه، فردّ الله عليهم ذلك، فلا ينافي قوله تعالى: وَلَوْ شَاء رَبُّكَ لَأمَنَ مَنْ فِي الأرض كُلُّهُمْ جَمِيعًا [يونس: ۹۹] ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَكِنِ اخْتَلَفُوا فَيتُهُمْ مَنْ آمَنَ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ كَفَرَ وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللهُ مَا اقْتَتَلُوا وَلَكِنَّ اللهَ يَفْعَلْ مَا يُرِيدُ ﴾ [البقرة:٢٥٣]، والحديث الصحيح الذي اتفق عليه السلف والخلف أن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن)). (۱) ولقد أحسن القائل: فما شئت كان وإن لم أشا وما شئت إن لم تشأ لم يكن وقد أجيب بأنه أنكر عليهم اعتقادهم أن مشيئة الله تعالى دليل على أمره به، أو أنكر عليهم معارضة شرعه وأمره الذي أرسل به رسله وأنزل به كتبه بقضائه وقدره، فجعلوا المشيئة العامة دافعة للأمر، فلم يذكروا المشيئة على جهة التوحيد، وإنما ذكروها معارضين بها لأمره دافعين بها لشرعه كفعل الزنادقة وجهال الملاحدة إذا أمروا أو نهوا احتجوا بالقدر. وقد احتج سارق على عمر رضي الله عنه بالقدر، قال: «فأنا أقطع يدك بقضاء الله وقدره». ويشهد لذلك قوله :تعالى وكذلِكَ كَذَبَ الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِهِمْ حَتَّى ذَا قُوا بَأْسَنَا قُلْ هَلْ عِنْدَكُمْ مِنْ عِلْمٍ فَتُخْرِجُوهُ لَنَا إِنْ تَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا الظَّنَّ وَإِنْ أَنْتُمْ إِلَّا تَخْرُصُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٤٨] . والحاصل أن قولهم كلمة حق أريد بها الباطل. وأما قول إبليس : رَبِّ بِمَا أَغْوَيْتَنِي ﴾ [الحجر: ٣٩] ، فإنما ذم على احتجاجه بالقدر لا اعترافه بالقدر وإثباته له ولهذا قالوا إنه أعرف بالله من المعتزلي لمطابقة قوله سبحانه وتعالى: يُضِلُّ اللهُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ، أي عدلا ، وَيَهْدِى مَنْ تَشَاءُ ﴾ [المدثر: ۳۱]، أي فضلا، وقوله تعالى:
If it is said: This is problematic because of His statement: 'Those who associated partners will say: If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners, nor our fathers, nor would we have forbidden anything...' [al-An'am 6:148], and His statement: 'And those who associated partners said: If Allah had willed, we would not have worshipped anything besides Him, neither we nor our fathers, nor would we have forbidden anything besides Him...' [an-Nahl 16:35], and His statement: 'If the Most Merciful had willed, we would not have worshipped them. They have no knowledge of that; they are only conjecturing' [az-Zukhruf 43:20], i.e., lying or guessing and imagining. So Allah blamed them for making shirk occur from them due to Allah's will. And likewise He blamed Iblis when he attributed misguidance to Allah, saying: 'My Lord, because You have led me astray, I will surely adorn for them [the path of sin] on earth' [al-Hijr 15:39]. The answer: He denounced them because they used His will as evidence of His approval and love, and said: If He disliked and hated that, He would not have willed it. So they made Allah's will evidence of His pleasure, and Allah refuted that. That does not contradict His statement: 'And if your Lord had willed, all those on earth would have believed entirely' [Yunus 10:99], and His statement: 'But they differed, and among them were those who believed and those who disbelieved. And if Allah had willed, they would not have fought; but Allah does what He intends' [al-Baqarah 2:253], and the authentic hadith agreed upon by the predecessors and successors: 'What Allah wills is, and what He does not will is not.' And the poet said well: 'What You will is, even if I do not will; what I will is not unless You will it.' And it has been answered that He denounced them for their belief that Allah's will indicates His command, or He denounced them for opposing His law and command which He sent with His messengers and revealed in His books with His decree and destiny, making the universal will a daf' (repelling) of the command. So they did not mention will in the manner of tawhid, but rather mentioned it opposing His command and repelling His law, like the act of zanadiqa (heretics) and ignorant atheists when they are commanded or prohibited, they argue by destiny. A thief argued before Umar (radiyallahu anhu) by destiny, saying: 'I cut your hand by Allah's decree and destiny.' And that is witnessed by His statement: 'Thus those before them denied until they tasted Our might. Say: Do you have any knowledge that you can produce for us? You follow nothing but conjecture, and you are only guessing' [al-An'am 6:148]. The conclusion is that their statement is a word of truth by which falsehood is intended. As for Iblis's statement: 'My Lord, because You have led me astray' [al-Hijr 15:39], he was blamed for arguing by destiny, not for acknowledging destiny and affirming it. For this reason they said that he knew Allah better than the Mu'tazilite, in accordance with His statement: 'Allah misguides whom He wills, in justice, and guides whom He wills, in virtue' [al-Muddaththir 74:31], and His statement: ...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a sustained objection-and-answer unit addressing a key Quranic evidence that might seem to support the determinist (jabri) view. The objection: God criticized polytheists for saying 'If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners'—that seems to deny that divine will is an excuse. Similarly, Iblis blamed God for leading him astray. How can we then hold humans accountable? The answer unfolds in multiple layers. First, God denounced them because they misinterpreted His will as indicating His approval; they thought that if God willed an act, He must be pleased with it. God refuted that equation. Second, this does not contradict other verses affirming universal divine will (e.g., Yunus 10:99) or the hadith 'What Allah wills is, what He does not will is not.' Third, the real problem was that they used God's will to argue against His command and law, as if the universal will (al-mashī'a al-‘āmma) negates the obligation to obey. This is the method of heretics: when commanded, they argue by predestination. The story of the thief with Umar illustrates this—the thief's excuse was rejected. Fourth, Iblis was blamed not for affirming predestination but for using it as an excuse. In fact, the salaf said Iblis knew Allah better than the Mu'tazila who deny divine guidance and misguidance. The passage concludes that their statement 'If Allah had willed' is a word of truth intended for falsehood (kalima ḥaqq urīda bihā bāṭil).

Key Terms
مشيئة الله
رضى
شرك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God wills an act, then He must be pleased with it and it is therefore permissible.
Correction: God may will an act without being pleased with it; His will encompasses both good and evil in terms of creation, but His approval is only for good.

Checkpoint
Why did God blame the polytheists for saying 'If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners'?
A) Because they denied divine will.
B) Because they used divine will as evidence of His approval.
C) Because they attributed shirk to God.
D) Because they claimed God wills evil.

Key Takeaway
Using God's will to claim His approval is a misuse that God condemns.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself excusing a sin by thinking 'If God didn’t want it, it wouldn’t have happened,' are you confusing His will with His approval? How will you guard your heart from this trap starting today?
?
Can you recall a moment where you used God’s decree to avoid taking responsibility? What would it look like to fully own your actions while still trusting His sovereignty?
?
If someone you love is sliding into sin using the excuse of qadar, will you have the courage to lovingly correct them with the truth from this lesson? What’s the first step you’ll take?

Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
Divine Will Does Not Negate Divine Command
The second part of the answer: divine will and command are distinct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the polytheists' argument is refuted by distinguishing universal will from the obligation to obey God's command.

Core Idea
God's universal will is not a license to disobey His commands.

The polytheists' error runs deeper than misusing will as approval. They pitted God's decree against His law, as if the former nullifies the latter. This lesson explores how the classical answer shows that citing qadar to oppose sharia is the way of heretics, as illustrated by the story of the thief and Umar.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses that affirm universal divine will
Read the Quranic verses and hadith that affirm everything happens by God's will.
These show that the polytheists' premise is correct.
2
Understand the second answer
The author says God denounced them for opposing His command with His decree.
They used will to repudiate the obligation to obey.
3
Examine the analogy of heretics and the thief
The method is like heretics who argue by qadar when commanded. The thief before Umar illustrates this.
4
Conclude with the key insight
Their statement is a word of truth intended for falsehood.
The phrase is true in itself but used to deny God's law.

(۱) ولقد أحسن القائل: فما شئت كان وإن لم أشا وما شئت إن لم تشأ لم يكن وقد أجيب بأنه أنكر عليهم اعتقادهم أن مشيئة الله تعالى دليل على أمره به، أو أنكر عليهم معارضة شرعه وأمره الذي أرسل به رسله وأنزل به كتبه بقضائه وقدره، فجعلوا المشيئة العامة دافعة للأمر، فلم يذكروا المشيئة على جهة التوحيد، وإنما ذكروها معارضين بها لأمره دافعين بها لشرعه كفعل الزنادقة وجهال الملاحدة إذا أمروا أو نهوا احتجوا بالقدر. وقد احتج سارق على عمر رضي الله عنه بالقدر، قال: «فأنا أقطع يدك بقضاء الله وقدره». ويشهد لذلك قوله :تعالى وكذلِكَ كَذَبَ الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِهِمْ حَتَّى ذَا قُوا بَأْسَنَا قُلْ هَلْ عِنْدَكُمْ مِنْ عِلْمٍ فَتُخْرِجُوهُ لَنَا إِنْ تَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا الظَّنَّ وَإِنْ أَنْتُمْ إِلَّا تَخْرُصُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٤٨] . والحاصل أن قولهم كلمة حق أريد بها الباطل. وأما قول إبليس : رَبِّ بِمَا أَغْوَيْتَنِي ﴾ [الحجر: ٣٩] ، فإنما ذم على احتجاجه بالقدر لا اعترافه بالقدر وإثباته له ولهذا قالوا إنه أعرف بالله من المعتزلي لمطابقة قوله سبحانه وتعالى: يُضِلُّ اللهُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ، أي عدلا ، وَيَهْدِى مَنْ تَشَاءُ ﴾ [المدثر: ۳۱]، أي فضلا، وقوله تعالى:

Commentary
This passage is a sustained objection-and-answer unit addressing a key Quranic evidence that might seem to support the determinist (jabri) view. The objection: God criticized polytheists for saying 'If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners'—that seems to deny that divine will is an excuse. First, God denounced them because they misinterpreted His will as indicating His approval; they thought that if God willed an act, He must be pleased with it. God refuted that equation. Third, the real problem was that they used God's will to argue against His command and law, as if the universal will (al-mashī'a al-‘āmma) negates the obligation to obey. This is the method of heretics: when commanded, they argue by predestination. The story of the thief with Umar illustrates this—the thief's excuse was rejected. Fourth, Iblis was blamed not for affirming predestination but for using it as an excuse. In fact, the salaf said Iblis knew Allah better than the Mu'tazila who deny divine guidance and misguidance. The passage concludes that their statement 'If Allah had willed' is a word of truth intended for falsehood (kalima ḥaqq urīda bihā bāṭil).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If everything is by God's will, then human choices and commands are irrelevant.
Correction: God's universal will does not cancel His commands; humans are still accountable and must obey the law.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the polytheists' error regarding the relationship between God's will and His command?
A) They denied God's will.
B) They used God's will to oppose His command.
C) They claimed God's will is limited.
D) They said God's command is unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
Using God's decree to escape His commands is a falsehood, even if the words sound pious.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used the phrase 'it was written' to avoid taking responsibility for a sin or a missed obligation? How does this lesson expose that as a misuse of truth?
?
When you find yourself slipping in obedience, do you inwardly comfort yourself with thoughts like 'Allah wills whatever He wills' instead of immediately repenting? What would it cost you to abandon that comfort?
?
The polytheists spoke a true statement ('if Allah had willed') but with a false intention. Where in your life might you be using a true Islamic concept to justify disobedience or delay in action?

Divine Decree
intermediate
7 min
Iblis: Qur'anic Model of Qadar Argument and Its Refutation
The answer regarding Iblis and the Ahl al-Sunna stance on qadar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Iblis was blamed for his qadar argument and how the salaf viewed him as more knowledgeable than the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Iblis was not blamed for affirming qadar but for using it as an excuse.

Iblis said, 'My Lord, because You have led me astray...' This seems to blame God. Yet the classical scholars say Iblis knew Allah better than the Mu'tazila. This lesson unpacks the distinction between accepting qadar and using it to evade responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read Iblis's statement and the blame
Read Iblis's statement from the Quran and note that he was blamed.
2
Understand the response
The passage says he was blamed for arguing by qadar, not for acknowledging it.
3
Note the salaf's assessment
The salaf said Iblis knew Allah better than the Mu'tazila because he affirmed divine guidance and misguidance.
This contrasts with the Mu'tazila who deny that Allah creates misguidance.
4
Connect to the Quranic principle
The verse shows that misguidance is just and guidance is grace.

فإن قيل: يشكل على هذا قوله تعالى: سَيَقُولُ الَّذِينَ اشْرَكُوا لَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا أَشْرَكْنَا وَ لَا آبَاؤُنَا وَلَا حَرَّمْنَا مِن شَى الآية [الأنعام: ١٤٨]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَالَ الَّذِينَ اشْرَ كَوْا لَوْ شَاء اللَّهُ مَا عَبَدَنَا مِنْ دُونِهِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ نَحْنُ وَلَا أَبَا وَنَا وَ لَا حَرَّ مُنَا مِنْ دُونِهِ مِنْ شَيْ﴾ الآية [النحل : ٣٥]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَوْشَاء الرَّحْمٰنُ مَا عَبَدُ ذَهُمْ مَا لَهُمْ بِذلِكَ مِنْ عِلْمٍ إِنْ هُمْ أَلَّا يَخْرُصُونَ ﴾ [الزخرف: ۲۰] ، أي يكذبون أو يظنون ويتوهمون فقد ذمهم الله تعالى حيث جعلوا الشرك كائنا منهم لمشيئة الله. وكذلك ذم إبليس حيث أضاف الإغواء إلى الله تعالى إذ قال : رب بما أغويتني لأزينن لهم في الأرض [ الحجر : ٣٩]. والجواب: أنه أنكر عليهم ذلك لأنهم احتجوا بمشيئته على رضاه ومحبته وقالوا: لو كره ذلك وسخط لما شاء، فجعلوا مشيئة الله دليل رضاه، فردّ الله عليهم ذلك، فلا ينافي قوله تعالى: وَلَوْ شَاء رَبُّكَ لَأمَنَ مَنْ فِي الأرض كُلُّهُمْ جَمِيعًا [يونس: ۹۹] ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَكِنِ اخْتَلَفُوا فَيتُهُمْ مَنْ آمَنَ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ كَفَرَ وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللهُ مَا اقْتَتَلُوا وَلَكِنَّ اللهَ يَفْعَلْ مَا يُرِيدُ ﴾ [البقرة:٢٥٣]، والحديث الصحيح الذي اتفق عليه السلف والخلف أن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن)). (۱) ولقد أحسن القائل: فما شئت كان وإن لم أشا وما شئت إن لم تشأ لم يكن وقد أجيب بأنه أنكر عليهم اعتقادهم أن مشيئة الله تعالى دليل على أمره به، أو أنكر عليهم معارضة شرعه وأمره الذي أرسل به رسله وأنزل به كتبه بقضائه وقدره، فجعلوا المشيئة العامة دافعة للأمر، فلم يذكروا المشيئة على جهة التوحيد، وإنما ذكروها معارضين بها لأمره دافعين بها لشرعه كفعل الزنادقة وجهال الملاحدة إذا أمروا أو نهوا احتجوا بالقدر. وقد احتج سارق على عمر رضي الله عنه بالقدر، قال: «فأنا أقطع يدك بقضاء الله وقدره». ويشهد لذلك قوله :تعالى وكذلِكَ كَذَبَ الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِهِمْ حَتَّى ذَا قُوا بَأْسَنَا قُلْ هَلْ عِنْدَكُمْ مِنْ عِلْمٍ فَتُخْرِجُوهُ لَنَا إِنْ تَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا الظَّنَّ وَإِنْ أَنْتُمْ إِلَّا تَخْرُصُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٤٨] . والحاصل أن قولهم كلمة حق أريد بها الباطل. وأما قول إبليس : رَبِّ بِمَا أَغْوَيْتَنِي ﴾ [الحجر: ٣٩] ، فإنما ذم على احتجاجه بالقدر لا اعترافه بالقدر وإثباته له ولهذا قالوا إنه أعرف بالله من المعتزلي لمطابقة قوله سبحانه وتعالى: يُضِلُّ اللهُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ، أي عدلا ، وَيَهْدِى مَنْ تَشَاءُ ﴾ [المدثر: ۳۱]، أي فضلا، وقوله تعالى:
If it is said: This is problematic because of His statement: 'Those who associated partners will say: If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners, nor our fathers, nor would we have forbidden anything...' [al-An'am 6:148], and His statement: 'And those who associated partners said: If Allah had willed, we would not have worshipped anything besides Him, neither we nor our fathers, nor would we have forbidden anything besides Him...' [an-Nahl 16:35], and His statement: 'If the Most Merciful had willed, we would not have worshipped them. They have no knowledge of that; they are only conjecturing' [az-Zukhruf 43:20], i.e., lying or guessing and imagining. So Allah blamed them for making shirk occur from them due to Allah's will. And likewise He blamed Iblis when he attributed misguidance to Allah, saying: 'My Lord, because You have led me astray, I will surely adorn for them [the path of sin] on earth' [al-Hijr 15:39]. The answer: He denounced them because they used His will as evidence of His approval and love, and said: If He disliked and hated that, He would not have willed it. So they made Allah's will evidence of His pleasure, and Allah refuted that. That does not contradict His statement: 'And if your Lord had willed, all those on earth would have believed entirely' [Yunus 10:99], and His statement: 'But they differed, and among them were those who believed and those who disbelieved. And if Allah had willed, they would not have fought; but Allah does what He intends' [al-Baqarah 2:253], and the authentic hadith agreed upon by the predecessors and successors: 'What Allah wills is, and what He does not will is not.' And the poet said well: 'What You will is, even if I do not will; what I will is not unless You will it.' And it has been answered that He denounced them for their belief that Allah's will indicates His command, or He denounced them for opposing His law and command which He sent with His messengers and revealed in His books with His decree and destiny, making the universal will a daf' (repelling) of the command. So they did not mention will in the manner of tawhid, but rather mentioned it opposing His command and repelling His law, like the act of zanadiqa (heretics) and ignorant atheists when they are commanded or prohibited, they argue by destiny. A thief argued before Umar (radiyallahu anhu) by destiny, saying: 'I cut your hand by Allah's decree and destiny.' And that is witnessed by His statement: 'Thus those before them denied until they tasted Our might. Say: Do you have any knowledge that you can produce for us? You follow nothing but conjecture, and you are only guessing' [al-An'am 6:148]. The conclusion is that their statement is a word of truth by which falsehood is intended. As for Iblis's statement: 'My Lord, because You have led me astray' [al-Hijr 15:39], he was blamed for arguing by destiny, not for acknowledging destiny and affirming it. For this reason they said that he knew Allah better than the Mu'tazilite, in accordance with His statement: 'Allah misguides whom He wills, in justice, and guides whom He wills, in virtue' [al-Muddaththir 74:31], and His statement: ...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a sustained objection-and-answer unit addressing a key Quranic evidence that might seem to support the determinist (jabri) view. The objection: God criticized polytheists for saying 'If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners'—that seems to deny that divine will is an excuse. Similarly, Iblis blamed God for leading him astray. How can we then hold humans accountable? The answer unfolds in multiple layers. First, God denounced them because they misinterpreted His will as indicating His approval; they thought that if God willed an act, He must be pleased with it. God refuted that equation. Second, this does not contradict other verses affirming universal divine will (e.g., Yunus 10:99) or the hadith 'What Allah wills is, what He does not will is not.' Third, the real problem was that they used God's will to argue against His command and law, as if the universal will (al-mashī'a al-‘āmma) negates the obligation to obey. This is the method of heretics: when commanded, they argue by predestination. The story of the thief with Umar illustrates this—the thief's excuse was rejected. Fourth, Iblis was blamed not for affirming predestination but for using it as an excuse. In fact, the salaf said Iblis knew Allah better than the Mu'tazila who deny divine guidance and misguidance. The passage concludes that their statement 'If Allah had willed' is a word of truth intended for falsehood (kalima ḥaqq urīda bihā bāṭil).

Key Terms
إبليس
إغواء
معتزلي
إضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iblis's statement proves that God is responsible for his sin.
Correction: Iblis was blamed for using qadar to excuse his sin, not for affirming that God is the ultimate creator of actions.

Checkpoint
Why did the salaf say Iblis knew Allah better than the Mu'tazila?
A) Because Iblis repented and the Mu'tazila did not.
B) Because Iblis affirmed divine guidance and misguidance, while the Mu'tazila deny it.
C) Because Iblis was an angel and the Mu'tazila are humans.
D) Because Iblis was more knowledgeable about theology.

Key Takeaway
Affirming qadar is part of faith; using it to blame God is sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'It was meant to be' or 'Allah made me do it' — just as Iblis did? What would it cost you to stop using qadar as a shield and instead own your choices fully before Allah?
?
Iblis acknowledged qadar — he knew Allah leads astray — yet that knowledge did not save him because he used it to justify rebellion. Is there an area of your life where your knowledge of Islam remains theoretical, disconnected from obedience? What is that one truth you know but refuse to act on?
?
The early scholars said Iblis knew Allah better than the Mu'tazila. How terrifying is it that correct belief about qadar can coexist with being the worst of creation? What is the difference between your faith and Iblis's faith — a difference only you and Allah know?

Divine Guidance and the Hadith of Adam's Predestination Argument
Commentator explains divine guidance and the proper use of qadr in the Hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic perspective on using divine predestination as an excuse for sin, particularly in light of the Hadith of Adam and Moses.

Core Idea
Predestination is only a valid comfort after repentance, not an excuse during sin.

This lesson explores a crucial aspect of the doctrine of qadar: how to understand the Hadith where Adam uses predestination to answer Moses. The commentator clarifies that invoking qadr is only permissible after repentance, not while committing the sin. We will examine the Quranic foundation and the hadith's proper application.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Begin by reading the two verses from Surah Al-Isra and Surah Az-Zumar that establish Allah's absolute control over guidance and misguidance.
2
Read the Hadith of Adam and Moses
Read the hadith where Adam responds to Moses by referencing predestination. Consider the context of the conversation.
3
Understand the commentator's distinction
The commentator explains that using qadr as an excuse is only valid after repentance, not at the time of sin. Reflect on why this distinction is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ يَهْدِ اللَّهُ فَهُوَ الْمُهْتَدِ﴾ [الإسراء: ۹۷]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يُضْلِلِ اللهُ فَمَالَهُ مِنْ هَادٍ﴾ [الزمر: ٣٦]. وأما قول آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام في جواب موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام: ((أفتلومني على أن عملت عملا قد كتبه الله علي أن أعمله قبل أن يخلقني بأربعين سنة؟)). فمبني على أن لا اعتراض على العاصي بعد توبته ورجوعه إلى طاعته وأن له حينئذ أن يتعلق بالقضاء والقدر، بل يجب أن يعتقد أن معصيته كانت مقدّرة قبل خلقه وليس له حين مباشرته قبل تحقق توبته أن يتشبث بالقضاء والقدر في قضيته فإنه حينئذ كالمعارض لنهيه سبحانه عن معصيته وأمره بطاعته، ولا راد لقضائه ولا معقب لحكمه ولا غالب لأمره.
"And whomsoever Allah guides, he is the guided one" [Al-Isra 17:97], and His saying most high: "And whomsoever Allah leads astray, for him there is no guide" [Az-Zumar 39:36]. And as for the saying of Adam (peace be upon him) in answer to Moses (peace be upon him): "Do you blame me for an action which Allah decreed for me to do before He created me by forty years?" — it is based on the fact that there is no objection against the sinner after his repentance and his return to obedience, and that then he may cling to the decree and predestination; rather, he must believe that his sin was decreed before his creation, while at the time of committing it before his repentance is realized, he may not cling to the decree and predestination in his case, for then he is like one objecting to His (glorified and exalted be He) prohibition of his sin and command to obedience. And there is no repeller of His decree, no reviser of His judgment, and no one prevailing over His command.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of divine guidance and predestination. It begins by citing two Qur'anic verses establishing that Allah alone guides and misguides whom He wills. Then it presents the hadith in which Adam argues to Moses that his sin was written before his creation. The commentator explains that Adam's argument is valid only after repentance; before repentance, one cannot use divine decree as an excuse for sin, because that would be objecting to Allah's prohibition. The passage emphasizes the absolute sovereignty of Allah's decree.

Key Terms
القدر (al-qadr)
القضاء (al-qada')
الهداية (al-hidaya)
الضلال (al-dalal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that predestination can be used as an excuse to sin at the moment of committing it.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that using qadr as an excuse is only valid after repentance, not during the sin itself, because doing so would be objecting to Allah's prohibition.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, when can a person use divine predestination as an excuse for a sin?
A) At the moment of committing the sin
B) After repentance and returning to obedience
C) Never, because predestination does not apply to sins
D) Only if the sin was not known

Key Takeaway
The Hadith of Adam and Moses teaches that invoking divine decree is only appropriate after repentance, not as an excuse for ongoing sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you find yourself quickly using the excuse 'It was written for me' instead of immediately repenting? How will you change this after learning that such an excuse is only valid after repentance?
?
Have you ever felt that acknowledging Allah's decree after repentance is an admission of defeat? This lesson teaches it is a comfort. What prevents you from accepting that comfort?
?
Imagine you are standing before Allah with a sin you justified using qadr. What would you say to His prohibition and command? Will you now commit to never using predestination as an excuse during sin?

Silence Before the Depths of Qadr
Wahb ibn Munabbih's reflection on qadr and the hadith commanding silence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early scholars advised silence about the inner reality of divine decree (qadr) and how this silence relates to belief in it.

Core Idea
True knowledge of qadr leads to humility, not endless speech.

This lesson presents a profound reflection from Wahb ibn Munabbih and a prophetic directive. Together, they teach that the most knowledgeable people about qadr are those who refrain from delving into its ultimate reality, while the ignorant speak most. Understanding this helps us balance belief in qadr with proper intellectual humility.

Guided Path
1
Read Wahb's reflection
Read the quote from Wahb ibn Munabbih carefully. Notice his repeated perplexity and his observation about the most and least knowledgeable.
Consider why looking into qadr would lead to perplexity.
2
Study the hadith and its commentary
Read the hadith and the commentator's clarification. Understand that the command to be silent is about explaining the reality of qadr, not about rejecting or doubting it.
This distinction is crucial.
3
Reflect on the lesson's application
Ask yourself: How does this teaching guide our approach to discussing qadr? What should we affirm, and what should we refrain from exploring?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن وهب بن منبه أنه قال: نظرت في القدر فتحيرت ثم نظرت فيه فتحيرت، ووجدت أعلم الناس بالقدر أكفهم عنه وأجهل الناس بالقدر أنطقهم فيه. ويؤيده قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ((وإذا ذكر القدر فأمسكوا)). يعني عن بيان حقيقته لا عن الإيمان به وحقيته.
And from Wahb ibn Munabbih that he said: I looked into qadr (predestination) and became perplexed, then I looked into it and became perplexed. And I found that the most knowledgeable people about qadr are those who refrain from it, and the most ignorant people about qadr are those who speak most about it. This is supported by his saying (peace and blessings be upon him): "When qadr is mentioned, then be silent" — meaning about explaining its reality, not about believing in it and affirming it.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a quote from Wahb ibn Munabbih expressing his perplexity about the topic of divine decree, and his observation that the more one knows about it, the more one refrains from speaking. It then cites a hadith commanding silence when qadr is mentioned. The commentator clarifies that this silence pertains to discussing its inner reality, not to belief in it.

Key Terms
القدر (al-qadr)
الإمساك (al-imasak)
الحقيقة (al-haqiqa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The command to be silent about qadr means we should not believe in it or discuss it at all.
Correction: The commentator explicitly clarifies that the silence pertains to explaining its inner reality, not to believing in it and affirming it. Belief in qadr is obligatory; it is the attempt to fully grasp its nature that is discouraged.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith "When qadr is mentioned, be silent" mean according to the commentator?
A) Do not believe in qadr at all
B) Do not speak about its inner reality, but do believe in it
C) Do not mention qadr in any context
D) Only scholars may speak about qadr

Key Takeaway
The most knowledgeable about qadr are those who refrain from discussing its reality, while affirming its truth and their own awe before it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter discussions about qadr, do you feel the urge to speak and explain, or do you find comfort in silence? What does your instinct reveal about your own understanding of Allah's decree?
?
Think of a situation where you tried to fully understand why something happened to you in terms of qadr. Did that lead you to contentment or to more confusion? How can you practice the silence that Wahb ibn Munabbih spoke of in that area of your life?
?
The Prophet commanded silence about the reality of qadr. In what ways have you crossed that boundary, and what steps can you take today to submit more fully to the mystery of Allah's decree?

Interpreting Good and Evil in the Verse
Commentator interprets the verse and refutes Qadariyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct interpretation of 'good' and 'evil' in Qur'an 4:78-79 and how it refutes the Qadariyya position.

Core Idea
Not all good and evil refer to moral actions; context distinguishes blessings from calamities.

In this passage, the commentator tackles a key verse often used in theological disputes about predestination. He presents the correct interpretation and shows why the Qadariyya cannot use it to support their denial of divine decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two interpretations offered for 'good' and 'evil'.
The most correct interpretation sees them as blessings and calamities.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Find where the commentator states the first (most correct) interpretation and the second (alternative) interpretation. Understand the difference.
3
Understand the refutation of the Qadariyya
The commentator gives two reasons why the Qadariyya cannot use verse 4:79. Follow the logic: they claim all actions from God, but the Qur'an distinguishes, and verse 4:78 says 'all is from God' regarding recompense, not actions.
This is key to preserving both divine decree and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن تُصِبْهُمْ حَسَنَةٌ يَقُوْلُوْا هَذِهِ مِنْ عِنْدِ اللهِ وَإِن تُصِبْهُمْ سَيِّئَةً يَقُوْلُوْا هَذِهِ مِنْ عِنْدِكَ الآية [النساء: ۷۸]، فالأصح أن المراد بالحسنة هنا النعمة وبالسيئة البلية، فلا حجة لنا ولا علينا، وقيل الحسنة الطاعة والسيئة المعصية، ومع هذا فليس للقدرية أن يحتجوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَصَابَكَ مِنْ سَيِّئَةٍ فَمِنْ نَّفْسِكَ﴾ [النساء: ٧٩]، فإنهم يقولون إن فعل العبد حسنة كانت أو سيئة فهو من الله، والقرآن قد فرق بينهما وهم لا يفرقون، ولأنه سبحانه قال: قُلْ كُلُّ مِنْ عِنْدِ اللهِ﴾ [النساء: ۷۸] فجعل الحسنات عند الله، وهم لا يقولون بذلك في الأعمال عند الله كما جعل السيئات من عند الله، بل في الجزاء.
And as for His saying most high: "If good befalls them, they say this is from God; and if evil befalls them, they say this is from you" [An-Nisa 4:78]. The most correct is that what is meant by 'good' here is blessing, and by 'evil' is calamity; so there is no argument for us or against us. And it is said: 'good' is obedience, and 'evil' is disobedience. Yet despite this, the Qadariyya have no right to argue with His saying most high: "Whatever evil befalls you is from yourself" [An-Nisa 4:79]. For they claim that the action of the slave, whether good or evil, is from God; but the Qur'an has distinguished between them while they do not distinguish. And because He (glorified and exalted be He) said: "Say, all is from God" [An-Nisa 4:78]; He placed good deeds with God, but they do not say that regarding actions as being from God, just as He placed evil actions as from Himself? Rather, in recompense (they are from Him).
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage discusses the interpretation of Qur'an 4:78-79. The commentator states the most correct interpretation is that 'good' means blessings and 'evil' means calamities, not moral good and evil. He then mentions an alternative interpretation. He refutes the Qadariyya sect who claim that all actions (good and evil) are from God, arguing that the Qur'an itself distinguishes between good and evil attributions. The verse 'Whatever evil befalls you is from yourself' is used to show that evil actions are attributed to the human, not God, while the verse 'All is from God' refers to the overall decree or to recompense.

Key Terms
الحسنة
السيئة
القدرية
النعمة
البلية
الجزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya think that verses 4:78-79 prove that humans create their own good and evil actions, thus denying divine decree.
Correction: The correct interpretation distinguishes blessings and calamities (not moral actions) and shows that 'all is from God' refers to recompense, not the actions themselves.

Checkpoint
According to the most correct interpretation mentioned, what do 'good' and 'evil' refer to in verse 4:78?
A) Obedience and disobedience
B) Blessings and calamities
C) Reward and punishment
D) Faith and disbelief

Key Takeaway
Sunni theologians clarify that 'good' in the verse refers to blessings and 'evil' to calamities, not moral good and evil, and thus the Qadariyya cannot claim support from these verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a calamity strikes you, do you immediately attribute it to God or to your own failings? How does this lesson's distinction between blessings and calamities challenge your gut reaction, and what would it mean for you to accept both as from God with patience?
?
Have you ever used the excuse that 'everything is from God' to avoid taking responsibility for your own sins? How does the commentator's refutation of the Qadariyya correct that mindset, and what concrete step will you take today to own your actions while still trusting God's decree?
?
The Qadariyya misused verses to deny God's absolute decree. Are there any verses you tend to reinterpret to fit your own comfort or avoid submitting to God's wisdom? What would it cost you to embrace the correct interpretation as taught by Ahl al-Sunnah, and are you willing to pay that price?

Reconciling 'All Is from God' and 'Evil from Yourself'
Question and answer reconciling two verses about the source of good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator reconciles the seemingly contradictory verses 'All is from God' and 'Evil from yourself' by distinguishing between general divine decrees and personal trials resulting from sin.

Core Idea
Good and evil both come from God, but personal calamities are tied to our own sins as justice and mercy.

This passage addresses a seeming contradiction in the Quran: one verse says everything is from God, another says evil befalls you from yourself. The commentator shows that these verses refer to different categories of events, harmonizing divine sovereignty with human accountability. By the end of this lesson, you will see how this distinction preserves both divine transcendence and personal responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the opening question that highlights the apparent conflict between the two verses. Notice that the objector assumes a contradiction.
The verses are 4:78 and 4:79.
2
Identify the two categories in the answer
The answer first lists general conditions (abundance, drought, victory, defeat) that are from God. Then it distinguishes personal calamities (evil, hardship) as from one's own soul.
3
Understand the purpose of personal calamities
The commentator explains that personal evils serve as punishment for sins or expiation. This shows divine justice and mercy within human responsibility.
4
Reflect on the reconciliation
Consider how this answer removes the contradiction: God decrees all, but the moral cause of personal suffering lies in human actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: كيف وجه الجمع بين قوله تعالى: ﴿قُل كُلّ مِنْ عِندِ اللهِ﴾ وبين قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمِن نَّفْسِكَ﴾؟ أجيب بأن الخصب والجدب والنصرة والهزيمة كلها من عند الله: وَمَا أَصَابَكَ مِنْ سَيِّئَةِ أي محنة وبلية فبذنب نفسك عقوبةً لك وكفارة لك كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَصَابَكُمْ مِنْ مُّصِيبَةٍ﴾
If it is said: How is reconciliation possible between His saying most high: "Say, all is from God" [An-Nisa 4:78] and His saying most high: "From yourself" [An-Nisa 4:79]? The answer is: abundance and drought, victory and defeat, all are from God. And whatever evil (i.e., hardship and calamity) befalls you, then it is from your own soul — a punishment for you and an expiation for you — just as Allah most high said: "And whatever affliction befalls you" [Ash-Shura 42:30].
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and answer regarding two seemingly contradictory verses. The objection asks how to reconcile 'All is from God' and 'Whatever evil befalls you is from yourself.' The answer explains that general conditions like abundance and victory are from God, while specific calamities are due to one's own sins, serving as punishment or expiation. This understanding harmonizes the two verses without compromising divine sovereignty or human responsibility.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verses 'All is from God' and 'Evil from yourself' directly contradict each other, implying God creates evil and humans are not responsible.
Correction: The commentator shows they refer to different categories: general conditions (abundance, drought, victory, defeat) are from God, while personal calamities are tied to one's own sins as punishment or expiation, thus preserving both divine sovereignty and human accountability.

B) It is a result of one's own sins as punishment or expiation
C) It is a test from Allah with no cause

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction between 'All is from God' and 'Evil from yourself' is resolved by understanding that general conditions are from God, while personal calamities are tied to one's own sins as punishment or expiation.

Two Interpretations of the Verse on Afflictions
Commentator explains two interpretations of the verse on afflictions and the rule for attributing actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two meanings of the verse 'For what your own hands have earned' and the rule for attributing actions to Allah.

Core Idea
Allah's creation of obedience is grace; of disobedience is justice.

This passage from the commentator unpacks a key Quranic verse about afflictions. It presents two complementary understandings: one focuses on human responsibility for sins, the other on how we should speak about Allah's actions. Grasping this distinction is essential for a balanced theology of good and evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the first meaning
Start by reading the Quranic verse and notice the first meaning, which is described as the one relied upon. The verse attributes afflictions to what our hands have earned.
The first meaning emphasizes human causality.
2
Understand the second meaning
The second meaning concerns the proper attribution of actions: obedience is attributed to Allah because it is pure good, while evil is not directly attributed to Him out of courtesy, even though all actions are created by Allah.
This maintains Allah's transcendence and justice.
3
Note the supporting verse
The commentator cites another verse: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they are questioned.' This underscores Allah's absolute sovereignty and wisdom.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Consider how the creation of actions (good and evil) is from Allah, but the blame for evil is attributed to the human self through acquisition (kasb). This avoids both fatalism and attributing evil to Allah directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَبِمَا كَسَبَتْ أَيْدِيكُمْ وَيَعْفُو عَنْ كَثِيرٍ [الشورى: 30] وهذا على المعنى الأول الذي هو المعول، وأما على المعنى الثاني، فالطاعة تنسب إلى الله تعالى؛ لأنها محض خير، والسيئة لا تنسب إلى الله تأدباً؛ لكونها في صورة شر، والكل من عند الله خلقاً، فخلق الطاعة فضل وخلق المعصية عدل: لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ [الأنبياء: 23].
ثم في قوله: فِي نَفْسِكَ من الفوائد أن العبد لا يطمئن إلى نفسه ولا يسكن إليها، فإن الشر كائن فيها لا يجيء إلا منها، ولا يشتغل بكلام الناس ولا ذمهم إذا أساؤوا إليه، فإن ذلك من السيئات التي أصابته، وهي إنما أصابته بذنوبه، فيرجع إلى الله ويستعيذ بالله من شر نفسه وسيئات عمله ويسأل الله أن يعينه على طاعته، فبذلك يحصل له كل خير ويندفع عنه كل شر ولهذا كان أنفع الدعاء طلب الهداية، فإنها الإعانة على الطاعة وترك المعصية.
For what your own hands have earned, and He pardons much [Ash-Shura: 30]. This is according to the first meaning which is relied upon. As for the second meaning, obedience is attributed to Allah because it is pure good, while the evil deed is not attributed to Allah out of propriety because it appears in the form of evil, and all is from Allah in terms of creation. So the creation of obedience is grace and the creation of disobedience is justice: He is not questioned about what He does, but they are questioned [Al-Anbiya: 23].
Then in His saying: 'In yourself' there are benefits: that the servant does not feel secure from himself nor rest content with it, for evil resides in it and only comes from it. He does not occupy himself with people's talk or blame when they harm him, for that is among the evil deeds that have afflicted him, and they only afflict him due to his sins. So he returns to Allah and seeks refuge with Allah from the evil of his own self and from the evil deeds of his actions, and asks Allah to help him in his obedience. Thus he attains every good and repels every evil, and therefore the most beneficial supplication is seeking guidance, for it is assistance in obedience and abandonment of disobedience.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the Quranic verse 'فَبِمَا كَسَبَتْ أَيْدِيكُمْ وَيَعْفُو عَنْ كَثِيرٍ' (And for what your own hands have earned, and He pardons much). The commentator presents two interpretations of this verse. The first and primary meaning is that afflictions result from our own actions. The second meaning concerns the attribution of actions: obedience is attributed to Allah as pure good, while sins are not directly attributed to Him out of respect, even though all things—both good and evil—are created by Allah. The creation of good is grace, and the creation of evil is justice, supported by the verse 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they are questioned.' Following this, the commentator draws a practical moral lesson from the phrase 'in yourself': the believer should never trust his own ego because evil resides within it. When others harm him, he should recognize it as a consequence of his own sins, and therefore turn to Allah, seeking refuge from the evil of his own self and his deeds, and asking for assistance in obedience. By doing so, he attains every good and repels every evil. Hence, the most beneficial supplication is seeking guidance (al-hidāyah), as it encompasses help in obeying Allah and abandoning sin.

Key Terms
كسب
طاعة
معصية
فضل
عدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think that since Allah creates all actions, evil deeds can be directly attributed to Allah.
Correction: While Allah creates all actions, out of propriety and due to the nature of evil, evil deeds are not attributed to Allah. They are attributed to the human self through acquisition.

Checkpoint
According to the second meaning, why is obedience attributed to Allah?
A) Because it is a command
B) Because it is pure good
C) Because it is forced
D) Because it is desired

Key Takeaway
Allah creates all actions, but obedience is attributed to Him as grace, while disobedience is attributed to the human self as justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you secretly attribute it to Allah's decree to avoid feeling responsible? After this lesson, how will you acknowledge your own earning while still affirming Allah's creation? What specific sin will you take ownership of today and repent from, without blaming Allah?
?
Think of a good deed you performed recently. Did you attribute it to your own effort or to Allah's grace? This lesson says obedience is pure good and should be attributed to Allah. Write down one concrete way you will consciously thank Allah for enabling that deed and make sure your heart remains free of pride.
?
The passage teaches that evil deeds are not attributed to Allah out of propriety. Yet, when calamity strikes, do you find yourself complaining to Allah about your fate? What does this lesson teach you about the proper response to trials? Commit to one phrase you will say next time you face hardship to reflect this understanding.

The Moral Lesson of Self-Blame and Seeking Guidance
Commentator draws moral lessons from the phrase 'in yourself' and concludes that guidance is the best supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a believer should not trust his own self and why seeking guidance is the most beneficial supplication.

Core Idea
The most beneficial supplication is seeking guidance.

The commentator next draws a practical moral from the phrase 'in yourself' in the verse. He explains that a believer should never feel secure from his own ego because evil resides within it. This leads to a profound lesson about turning to Allah and seeking His guidance, which is the key to all good.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on self-blame
The passage explains the benefits of the phrase 'in yourself'. It teaches that the servant should not feel secure from himself nor rest content with it.
2
Understand why evil comes from the self
Evil resides in the human self and only comes from it. This is why one should not be self-confident.
This is a key aspect of Islamic psychology.
3
Learn the proper response to harm from others
When others harm you, recognize it as a consequence of your own sins, not as a reason to blame them. Then return to Allah and seek refuge from the evil of your self and deeds.
4
Recognize the centrality of guidance
The passage concludes that the most beneficial supplication is seeking guidance (al-hidāyah), because it includes help in obeying Allah and abandoning sin.
This connects to the lesson's core idea.

Human Capacity and Divine Decree in Belief and Disbelief
Commentary explains creation free from disbelief and faith, divine address, and the roles of khidhlaan and tawfeeq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator reconciles human free choice with divine decree in the acts of disbelief and belief, using the concepts of khidhlaan and tawfeeq.

Core Idea
God creates humans with capacity, not predetermined belief, then holds them accountable.

This lesson examines a key passage from the commentary on Fiqh al-Akbar that addresses the delicate balance between human choice and divine decree. The commentator clarifies the meaning of being created free from kufr and iman, and how actions of disbelief and belief are attributed to both human choice and divine khidhlaan or tawfeeq. We will see that this position is supported by Quranic verses and prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the flow: creation free from both, then address, then the two outcomes.
2
Identify key concepts
Identify the terms 'free from disbelief and faith' (سليماً من الكفر والإيمان), 'khidhlaan' (خذلان), and 'tawfeeq' (توفيق). Understand how each relates to human action.
These are central to the Ash'ari understanding of divine decree.
3
Examine the proof texts
Look at the Quranic verses (64:2, 10:44, 10:60) and hadiths cited. Note how they support the commentary's points.
Verse 64:2 shows creation includes potential for both; 10:44 emphasizes no injustice; 10:60 highlights divine bounty.
4
Address the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that God's khidhlaan implies compulsion. The commentary explicitly states ‘by his choice’ (باختياره), showing human responsibility.
This distinction is crucial for avoiding fatalism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلق الخلق سليماً من الكفر والإيمان، ثم خاطبهم وأمرهم ونهاهم، فكفر من كفر بفعله وإنكاره وجحوده الحق بخذلان الله تعالى إياه، وآمن من آمن بفعله وإقراره وتصديقه بتوفيق الله تعالى إياه ونصرته له. (خلق) أي الله تعالى كما في نسخة (الخلق) أي المخلوقين (سليما من الكفر والإيمان أي سالما من آثار الكفران وأنوار الإيمان بأن جعلهم قابلين؛ لأن يقع منهم العصيان والإحسان كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿هُوَالَّذِي خَلَقَكُمْ فَمِنْكُمْ كَافِرُ مِنْكُمْ مُؤْمِنَ ﴾ [التغابن: ٢] أي في عالم الظهور والبيان ثم خاطبهم أي في وقت التكليف بالعبادة على لسان أرباب الرسالة وأصحاب السعادة (وأمرهم) أي بالإيمان والطاعة ونهاهم) أي عن الكفر والمعصية. فكفر من كفر بفعله) أي باختياره (وإنكاره) أي مع جهله وإصراره وجحوده) (الحق) أي مع عناده واستكباره، بخذلان الله تعالى أي بترك نصرته سبحانه (إياه) وعدم توفيقه لما يرضاه، وهو مقتضى عدله كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَظْلِمُ النَّاسَ شَيْئًا وَ لَكِنَّ النَّاسَ أَنْفُسَهُمْ يَظْلِمُونَ ﴾ [يونس: ٤٤]، وآمن من آمن بفعله أي بانقياده وإذعانه (وإقراره) أي بلسانه (وتصديقه) أي بجنانه على وفق أمر ومراده بتوفيق الله تعالى إياه ونصرته له أي فيما قدره وقضاه بمقتضى فضله كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَذُو فَضْلٍ عَلَى النَّاسِ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ لَا يَشْكُرُونَ ﴾ [يونس: ٦٠]، وهذا لا ينافي كونهما كافرا ومؤمنا في علم الله تعالى بحديث : (خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ولا أبالي، وخلقت هؤلاء للنار ولا أبالي)).(۱) وحديث: ((فرغ ربكم من العباد فريق في الجنة وفريق في السعير)).(٢)
He created the creation free from disbelief and faith, then He addressed them and commanded them and forbade them. So whoever disbelieved, disbelieved by his action and his denial and his rejection of the truth, with the abandonment (khidhlaan) of God Most High of him. And whoever believed, believed by his action and his affirmation and his attestation, with the success-giving (tawfeeq) of God Most High to him and His assistance to him. (He created) i.e., God Most High, as in a copy, (the creation) i.e., the creatures, (free from disbelief and faith) i.e., free from the effects of disbelief and the lights of faith, by making them capable (qaabilin) that disobedience and beneficence should occur from them, as God Most High said: 'He is the One who created you, and among you are disbelievers and among you are believers' [Quran 64:2], i.e., in the world of manifestation and clarification. (Then He addressed them) i.e., at the time of obligation (takleef) with worship, upon the tongues of the messengers and the people of happiness. (And He commanded them) i.e., with faith and obedience, (and forbade them) i.e., from disbelief and disobedience. (So whoever disbelieved, disbelieved by his action) i.e., by his choice, (and his denial) i.e., with his ignorance and insistence and rejection, (the truth) i.e., with his obstinacy and arrogance, (with the abandonment of God Most High) i.e., by His leaving of assistance, Most High, (of him) and His not giving him success for what pleases Him, and that is the requirement of His justice, as God Most High said: 'Indeed, God does not wrong people at all, but people wrong themselves' [Quran 10:44]. (And whoever believed, believed by his action) i.e., his submission and compliance, (and his affirmation) i.e., with his tongue, (and his attestation) i.e., with his heart, according to His command and desire, with the success-giving of God Most High to him and His assistance to him, i.e., in what He determined and decreed by virtue of His bounty, as God Most High said: 'Indeed, God is full of bounty to people, but most of them are not grateful' [Quran 10:60]. And this does not contradict their being disbeliever and believer in the knowledge of God Most High, due to the hadith: 'I created these for Paradise and I do not care, and I created these for the Fire and I do not care.' And the hadith: 'Your Lord has finished with the servants: a group in Paradise and a group in the Blaze.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage explains a statement from the matn (Fiqh al-Akbar) regarding the creation of humans in a state free from both disbelief and faith, and the subsequent divine command and prohibition. The commentator clarifies that 'free from disbelief and faith' means free from the effects (آثار) of disbelief and the lights (أنوار) of faith — i.e., humans are created with a neutral capacity (قابلين) to choose either. This is supported by Quran 64:2, which states that among people are believers and disbelievers, indicating that this distinction becomes manifest in this life. Then at the time of obligation (تكليف), God addressed them through messengers, commanding faith and obedience and forbidding disbelief and disobedience. The commentator then explains the mechanics of disbelief and faith: a person disbelieves by his own action (بفعله) and choice (باختياره), with denial and rejection of the truth, but this occurs with God's abandonment (خذلان) — meaning God withholds His assistance and success-giving — which is a manifestation of His justice, as God does not wrong anyone (Quran 10:44). Conversely, a person believes by his own action (submission, affirmation with tongue, attestation with heart), and this occurs with God's success-giving (توفيق) and assistance, which is a manifestation of His bounty (Quran 10:60). Finally, the commentator notes that this does not contradict the fact that God already knows who will be disbeliever and who will be believer, citing two hadiths: 'I created these for Paradise and I do not care, and I created these for the Fire and I do not care' and 'Your Lord has finished with the servants: a group in Paradise and a group in the Blaze.'

Key Terms
خلق
فطرة
كفر
إيمان
خذلان
توفيق
قضاء
قدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's abandonment (khidhlaan) of the disbeliever means God forces disbelief, negating human responsibility.
Correction: The commentary explicitly states that the disbeliever disbelieves 'by his action' and 'by his choice' (باختياره). God's khidhlaan is a withholding of assistance, not compulsion, and is just.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what does 'بفعله' (by his action) in 'disbelieved by his action' indicate?
A) That disbelief is created directly by God.
B) That the disbeliever chooses disbelief by his own will.
C) That disbelief is an illusion.
D) That the disbeliever has no responsibility.

Key Takeaway
Humans are created with a neutral capacity, choose disbelief or belief by their own will, but divine khidhlaan or tawfeeq accompanies these choices in accordance with God's justice and bounty, all within His eternal decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson says your faith is a result of both your own action and God's tawfeeq. Have you ever truly felt that your iman is a gift? If you take it for granted, what will you do today to express gratitude for that gift?
?
If disbelief stems from your own choice and God's abandonment, are you aware of how your daily choices might be leading you toward that state? What specific sin or negligence will you repent from this week to avoid being abandoned?
?
God's justice means He does not wrong anyone. When you face hardship or feel your faith weakening, do you blame God or examine your own actions? What is one thing you can change in your life right now to align better with His commands?

Creation Free from Disbelief and Belief
Commentary on the initial creation as neutral and the role of divine abandonment and assistance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that humans are created neutral (free from disbelief and faith), and that disbelief and faith occur through human action combined with divine abandonment or assistance, all within divine decree.

Core Idea
Humans are born neutral; faith and disbelief are earned by action, granted by God.

This lesson explains a foundational statement from Imam Abu Hanifa's Fiqh al-Akbar about the innate human disposition. The commentary clarifies that creation is initially neutral, and that disbelief and faith are results of human choice and divine will working together. It also shows that this does not conflict with predestination.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full Arabic text and its literal translation to get the complete picture of the commentary.
Notice that the passage includes Quranic verses and hadiths.
2
Understand the neutral creation
The commentary explains that humans are created free from the effects of disbelief and the lights of belief, but capable of both. This is the starting point.
The term 'سَلِيماً' indicates purity and neutrality.
3
Analyze the roles of abandonment and success
Disbelief occurs by the servant's own action with Allah's abandonment (khidhlan), which is withholding of assistance. Belief occurs by the servant's own action with Allah's granting of success (tawfiq). Both are requirements of justice and grace.
Quran 10:44 and 10:60 are cited to support these points.
4
Reflect on harmony with divine decree
The commentary notes that this does not contradict Allah's eternal knowledge and decree, citing hadiths about predestination.
This reconciles human responsibility with divine predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما فطر الله عليه الناس
خلق الخلق سليماً من الكفر والإيمان، ثم خاطبهم وأمرهم ونهاهم، فكفر من كفر بفعله وإنكاره وجحوده الحق بخذلان الله تعالى إياه، وآمن من آمن بفعله وإقراره وتصديقه بتوفيق الله تعالى إياه ونصرته له،
(خلق) أي الله تعالى كما في نسخة (الخلق) أي المخلوقين (سليما من الكفر والإيمان أي سالما من آثار الكفران وأنوار الإيمان بأن جعلهم قابلين؛ لأن يقع منهم العصيان والإحسان كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَكُمْ فَمِنْكُمْ كَافِرٌ وَمِنْكُمْ مُؤْمِنٌ﴾ [التغابن: ٢] أي في عالم الظهور والبيان ثم خاطبهم أي في وقت التكليف بالعبادة على لسان أرباب الرسالة وأصحاب السعادة (وأمرهم) أي بالإيمان والطاعة ونهاهم) أي عن الكفر والمعصية. فكفر من كفر بفعله) أي باختياره (وإنكاره) أي مع جهله وإصراره وجحوده) (الحق) أي مع عناده واستكباره، بخذلان الله تعالى أي بترك نصرته سبحانه (إياه) وعدم توفيقه لما يرضاه، وهو مقتضى عدله كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَظْلِمُ النَّاسَ شَيْئًا وَلَكِنَّ النَّاسَ أَنْفُسَهُمْ يَظْلِمُونَ﴾ [يونس: ٤٤]، وآمن من آمن بفعله أي بانقياده وإذعانه (وإقراره) أي بلسانه (وتصديقه) أي بجنانه على وفق أمر ومراده بتوفيق الله تعالى إياه ونصرته له أي فيما قدره وقضاه بمقتضى فضله كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَذُو فَضْلٍ عَلَى النَّاسِ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ لَا يَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [يونس: ٦٠]، وهذا لا ينافي كونهما كافرا ومؤمنا في علم الله تعالى بحديث: (خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ولا أبالي، وخلقت هؤلاء للنار ولا أبالي). وحديث: (فرغ ربكم من العباد فريق في الجنة وفريق في السعير).
What God has innately disposed people upon. He created creation free from disbelief and belief, then addressed them, commanded them, and forbade them. So whoever disbelieved disbelieved by his own action, denial, and rejection of the truth with Allah's abandonment of him; and whoever believed believed by his own action, affirmation, and attestation with Allah's granting of success to him and His assistance. (He created) meaning Allah, as in one copy, or (the creation) meaning the created beings, (free from disbelief and belief) meaning safe from the effects of disbelief and the lights of belief, by making them capable of obedience and disobedience occurring from them, as Allah said: 'It is He who created you, and among you is a disbeliever and among you is a believer' [Quran 64:2] in the world of manifestation and explanation. Then He addressed them at the time of obligation of worship through the tongues of the messengers and the people of happiness, (and commanded them) to faith and obedience, and (forbade them) from disbelief and sin. So whoever disbelieved, (by his own action) meaning by his choice, (and his denial) meaning with ignorance and persistence and rejection, (of the truth) meaning with obstinacy and arrogance, by Allah's abandonment meaning His withholding of His assistance from him and His not granting him success to what pleases Him, and that is a requirement of His justice, as Allah said: 'Indeed Allah does not wrong people at all, but people wrong themselves' [Quran 10:44]. And whoever believed, (by his own action) meaning by his submission and compliance, (and his affirmation) with his tongue, (and his attestation) with his heart, in accordance with His command and will, by Allah's granting of success to him and His assistance, meaning in what He decreed and ordained by His grace, as Allah said: 'Indeed Allah is full of bounty to people, but most of them are not grateful' [Quran 10:60]. And this does not contradict that they are disbeliever and believer in Allah's knowledge, according to the hadith: 'I created these for Paradise and I do not mind, and I created these for the Fire and I do not mind' and the hadith: 'Your Lord has finished with the servants: one group in Paradise and one group in the Blaze.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement from Fiqh al-Akbar about the primordial nature of humans. It begins by quoting the matn: 'What God has innately disposed people upon. He created creation free from disbelief and belief, then addressed them, commanded them, and forbade them...' The commentator then explains each part: 'He created' refers to Allah or the creation, meaning they were created neutral—free from the effects of disbelief and the lights of belief, but capable of both. Then God addressed them through messengers at the time of obligation. 'Whoever disbelieved disbelieved by his own action' means by his own choice, denial, and rejection, but this occurs 'with Allah's abandonment' (khidhlan)—that is, Allah's withholding of assistance and success, which is a requirement of His justice, as shown by Quran 10:44. Conversely, 'whoever believed believed by his own action'—submission, affirmation with the tongue, and attestation with the heart—by Allah's granting of success (tawfiq) and assistance, according to His decree and grace, as shown by Quran 10:60. Finally, the commentator notes that this does not contradict the fact that both are known in Allah's eternal knowledge, citing the hadiths about predestination: 'I created these for Paradise and I do not mind...' and 'Your Lord has finished with the servants.' Thus the passage affirms both human responsibility and divine decree.

سليماً من الكفر والإيمان (free from disbelief and faith)
خذلان (abandonment)
توفيق (success/granting of success)
فطرة (innate disposition)
قضاء وقدر (decree and destiny)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that disbelief and faith are forced by God without any human role.
Correction: This passage clarifies that they occur by the servant's own action (choice, denial, submission) but under God's permission, abandonment, or assistance, all within His decree.

Checkpoint

B) Allah's withholding of assistance and success from someone
C) Allah's punishment of a disbeliever
D) Allah's hatred of the disbeliever

Key Takeaway
Humans are created neutral; their eventual state of faith or disbelief is a combination of their own action and God's decree, demonstrating both divine justice and grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This lesson reminds you that you were created neutral – neither believer nor disbeliever. What have you done with that neutrality? Have you taken your faith for granted or blamed Allah for your shortcomings? How will you now embrace your personal responsibility before Him?

The Primordial Covenant and the Innate Faith of Humanity
Commentary on the primordial covenant and the fitra of Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the primordial covenant between Allah and humanity's first progeny, how it established an innate faith (fitra), and why every child is born upon this fitra.

Core Idea
Before birth, all souls acknowledged Allah's lordship, making faith an innate human disposition.

The text explains the famous narrative of the 'Day of Alast' when Allah extracted Adam's future descendants and addressed them. This passage from the commentary unpacks how that event produced a form of faith, either real or judgmental, and establishes that every human is born with an innate disposition (fitra) towards Islam. Understanding this shapes our view of human nature and divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic excerpt and its English translation carefully to grasp the flow.
2
Identify the key elements of the covenant
Look for the extraction, intellect, command, acknowledgment, and how it is described as faith.
3
Distinguish between real and judgmental faith
Notice the comment that their 'Yes' was considered faith, either real (haqiqi) or judgmental (hukmi). Ask: Why both categories?
This distinction affects how we view the faith of those before birth.
4
Connect the fitra to the covenant
Understand that 'being born upon that fitra' means everyone has this primordial acknowledgment as a starting point.
This explains the hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitra of Islam.'

He brought forth the progeny of Adam, peace be upon him, from his loins in the form of tiny ants, and gave them intellect, then addressed them and commanded them with belief and forbade them from disbelief, so they acknowledged His lordship, and that was from them faith, so they are born upon that innate disposition. For the comprehensive and definitive hadith is his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Act, for everyone is facilitated to that for which he was created.' (He brought forth the progeny of Adam) meaning generation after generation until the Day of Resurrection, (from his loins) meaning first, then brought forth from the loins of his sons and the chests of his daughters their offspring in the form of tiny ants—meaning like small ants, some white and some black—and they spread out to the right of Adam and his left. Then He gave them intellect and addressed them, meaning when He made them witness over themselves by His saying: 'Am I not your Lord? They said: Yes' [Quran 7:172]. (And He commanded them with belief) meaning and with goodness, and forbade them from (disbelief) meaning and ingratitude. (So they acknowledged His lordship) meaning and for themselves servitude, when they said 'Yes,' so that was from them—their saying 'Yes' that issued from them—(faith) meaning real or judgmental. So they are born upon that innate disposition, meaning as Allah said: 'The fitra of Allah upon which He created people' [Quran 30:30] and as the Prophet said: 'Every child is born upon the fitra of Islam, then his parents make him a Jew, Christian, or Magian until his tongue expresses it, either grateful or ungrateful.' And this is the meaning of His saying: 'Indeed We guided him to the way, either grateful or ungrateful' [Quran 76:3]. The summary is that the covenant is established by the Book—the saying of Allah: 'And when your Lord took from the children of Adam from their loins their descendants' [Quran 7:172]—and by the Sunnah, namely the confirmed hadith narrated in
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement from Fiqh al-Akbar regarding the extraction of Adam's progeny and the primordial covenant. It begins by quoting the matn: 'He brought forth the progeny of Adam from his loins in the form of tiny ants, gave them intellect, addressed them, commanded belief, and forbade disbelief; they acknowledged His lordship, and that was faith, so they are born upon that fitra.' The commentator then explains each element. First, the hadith 'Act, for everyone is facilitated to that for which he was created' is cited as a comprehensive principle. Then, 'He brought forth the progeny of Adam' means generation after generation; 'from his loins' first, then from the loins of his sons and the chests of his daughters, in the form of tiny ants (like small ants, some white, some black), spreading to Adam's right and left. He gave them intellect and addressed them at the time of the covenant (Quran 7:172). He commanded faith and goodness and forbade disbelief and ingratitude. They acknowledged lordship for Him and servitude for themselves by saying 'Yes.' That saying was faith—either 'real faith' (imani haqiqi) or 'judgmental faith' (imani hukmi). Thus they are born upon that fitra, as per Quran 30:30 and the hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitra of Islam...' until the tongue expresses gratitude or ingratitude (Quran 76:3). The conclusion is that the covenant is established by both the Book (Quran 7:172) and the Sunnah (the confirmed hadith that follows, though the page cuts off).
