Refuting the Jabriyya Claim of Compulsion
The author refutes the Jabriyya claim that all actions are forced by Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni refutation of the Jabriyya claim that all actions are forced by Allah, and how divine knowledge and command affirm human free will.

Core Idea
Human free will is real; Allah's command proves we are not forced.

The Jabriyya sect misread the hadith about creation for Paradise or Hell to mean that Allah compels all actions. In this passage, the author presents their claims and then refutes them using sound reasoning and Qur'anic verses. We will see how Ahl al-Sunna affirm human choice while maintaining divine sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Jabriyya claim
Read the first part of the passage where the author lists the Jabriyya assertions: Allah creates believers as believers, disbelievers as disbelievers, etc.
Note how extreme their view is — it removes all human agency.
2
See the Sunni response
The author presents the Sunni position: prophets and Iblis change state by their own choice; this does not contradict Allah's knowledge.
The key point is that divine foreknowledge does not cause the action.
3
Recognize the argument against compulsion
If compulsion were absolute, contradictory acts (like Iblis obeying or Abu Bakr sinning) would not occur — but they have the capacity to do either.
This shows the logical flaw in the Jabriyya position.
4
Examine the Qur'anic evidence
The author cites two verses: the command to believe (4:136) and the covenant (7:172). Commands imply the addressee can choose to comply.
These verses directly refute the idea of compulsion.
5
Grasp the key terms
Understand 'mukhtar' (free), 'mustati'' (capable), and 'tawfiq' (success from Allah) as they are central to the Sunni position.
Tawfiq is divine grace enabling the servant to choose good, not compulsion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخذ بظاهره الجبرية، فقالوا: إن الله تعالى خلق المؤمنين مؤمنين، وخلق الكافرين كافرين، وإبليس لم يزل كافرا، وأبو بكر وعمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما كانا مؤمنين قبل الإسلام، والأنبياء عليهم السلام كانوا أنبياء قبل الوحي، وكذا إخوة يوسف كانوا أنبياء وقت الكبائر. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة صاروا أنبياء بعد ذلك، وإبليس صار كافرا، وهذا لا ينافي كونه كافرا عند الله باعتبار تعلق علمه بأنه سيصير كافرا بعلمه ولو كان جبرا محضا لما صدر من إبليس طاعة ولا من أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما معصية، فبطل قولهم إن الكفار مجبورون على الكفر والمعصية، والمؤمنين مجبورون على الإيمان والطاعة بل نقول: إن العبد مختار مستطيع على الطاعة والمعصية وليس بمجبور، والتوفيق من الله تعالى كما يدل عليه قوله سبحانه: ﴿ آمِنُوا بِاللهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ﴾ [النساء: ١٣٦] ، فلو كانوا مؤمنين لما أمرهم بالإيمان ولما خاطبهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ اَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲].
And the Jabriyya took its apparent meaning, so they said: Verily Allah the Exalted created the believers as believers, and created the disbelievers as disbelievers, and Iblis was always a disbeliever, and Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, were believers before Islam, and the prophets, peace be upon them, were prophets before revelation, and likewise the brothers of Joseph were prophets at the time of major sins. And Ahl al-Sunna said: They became prophets after that, and Iblis became a disbeliever, and this does not contradict his being a disbeliever in Allah's view in consideration of the attachment of His knowledge that he would become a disbeliever by his own choice. And if it were pure compulsion, then no act of obedience would have issued from Iblis, nor any act of disobedience from Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them. So their statement that the disbelievers are forced upon disbelief and sin, and the believers are forced upon faith and obedience, is invalid. Rather we say: The servant is free and capable of obedience and disobedience, and he is not forced. And success (tawfiq) is from Allah the Exalted, as indicated by His sublime saying: 'Believe in Allah and His Messenger' (4:136). For if they were believers, He would not have commanded them to believe, nor would He have addressed them with His saying: 'Am I not your Lord?' (7:172).
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of the Jabriyya who took the hadith literally to mean complete compulsion. They claimed that Allah creates believers as believers and disbelievers as disbelievers, that Iblis was always a disbeliever, that Abu Bakr and ʿUmar were believers before Islam, and that prophets were prophets before revelation. Ahl al-Sunna respond that prophets became prophets after revelation, and Iblis became a disbeliever. This does not contradict Allah's prior knowledge. If it were pure compulsion, then no act of obedience from Iblis or disobedience from Abu Bakr and ʿUmar would have occurred. Thus, the Jabriyya claim that disbelievers are forced into disbelief is false. Instead, the servant is free and capable (mukhtār mustaṭīʿ) of obedience and disobedience, not forced. Success (tawfīq) comes from Allah, as indicated by the command 'Believe in Allah and His Messenger' (4:136) — if they were already believers, they would not be commanded. Similarly, the address 'Am I not your Lord?' (7:172) implies they could respond.

Key Terms
الجبرية
مختار
مستطيع
التوفيق
آمِنُوا بِاللهِ وَرَسُولِهِ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah's predestination means humans have no free will and are forced into actions.
Correction: The author shows that divine command and human capacity (istita'a) affirm free will. Allah's knowledge does not force actions; humans choose.

Checkpoint
What argument does the author use to refute the Jabriyya claim that believers are forced into faith?
A) The hadith about Adam's offspring.
B) The verse commanding belief: 'Believe in Allah and His Messenger'.
C) The fact that Iblis was a disbeliever from the beginning.
D) The intercession of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Allah's command to believe proves that humans have the capacity to choose faith, refuting the Jabriyya claim of compulsion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking 'it was written' or 'Allah made me do it' as an excuse? How does the author's example of Iblis and the Companions force you to recognize that your choices are your own? What sin will you now stop excusing and actively fight?
?
If you truly believe that you are not forced, why do you still choose disobedience when you know it displeases Allah? What deep desire in your heart overcomes your faith? What will you do today to make obeying Allah your priority over that desire?
?
The author says that success (tawfiq) comes from Allah. Do you pray for tawfiq before every act of obedience? Reflect on the last time you succeeded in avoiding a sin: did you thank Allah for enabling you? What one action will you commit to thanking Him for daily?

Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
God Does Not Compel: The Balance of Divine Creation and Human Acquisition
Commentator explains the creedal statement on divine non-compulsion and human acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God does not compel anyone to disbelief or faith, but creates actions in the heart accompanied by the servant’s choice and acquisition (kasb), reconciling divine sovereignty with human responsibility.

Core Idea
God creates our actions, but we earn them through choice and acquisition.

This lesson unpacks a central creedal statement: God does not compel anyone to disbelief or faith. The commentator clarifies that while God creates all actions, they are accompanied by the servant's free choice and acquisition. This resolves the apparent tension between divine omnipotence and human responsibility. Through examples and Quranic proofs, we see how faith becomes beloved to believers and disbelief desired by disbelievers, all under God’s grace and justice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of 'not compelling'
Read the opening definition where the commentator explains the linguistic meaning and the theological point: God does not overpower anyone to disbelief or faith.
Note the phrasing 'accompanied by choice and acquisition'.
2
Analyze the examples of coercion and hypocrisy
Study the examples of the coerced believer and the hypocrite to see how outward action and inward conviction can differ, and why the disbeliever is not excused.
This illustrates the concept of kasb.
3
Reflect on divine grace and justice
Examine the Quranic verses and the commentator's conclusion that God’s grace makes faith beloved, and His justice withholds guidance from some, yet He is not questioned.
This connects to the secrets of qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ولم يُجبر) بضم الياء وكسر الباء، أي لم يقهر الله أحداً من خلقه على الكفر وعلى الإيمان) وفي نسخة ولا على الإيمان ، والمعنى أن الله تعالى لا يخلق الطاعة والمعصية في قلب العبد بطريق الجبر والغلبة، بل يخلقهما في قلبه مقرونا باختيار العبد وكسبه، فإن المكره على عمل هو الذي إذا عمل ذلك العمل يكرهه في الأصل، وكان المختار عنده أن لا يعمله فإنه عنده كالذليل كالمؤمن إذا أكره على إجراء كلمة الكفر فأجراها بظاهر البيان وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان، وكالمنافق حيث يجري الإيمان على اللسان وقلبه مشحون بالكفر، فليس الكافر في كفره معذوراً، ولا المؤمن في إيمانه مجبوراً، بل الإيمان محبوب للمؤمنين، كما أن الكفر مطلوب للكافرين، وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: كُلُّ حِزْبِ بِمَا لَدَيْهِمْ فَرِحُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون:٥٣]. غاية الأمر أن الله تعالى بفضله حبّب إلينا الإيمان وزيّن في قلوبنا الإحسان وكره إلينا الكفر والفسوق والعصيان والحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا وما كنا لنهتدي لولا أن هدانا الله، وبعدله ترك هداية أهل الكفر والكفران وحبّب إليهم العصيان وكره لديهم الإيمان، فسبحانه سبحانه، يُضِلُّ اللَّهُ مَنْ يَشَآءُ وَ يَهْدِى مَنْ يَشَاءُ [المدثر : ۳۱]، ﴿ وَمَن يُضْلِلِ اللَّهُ فَمَالَهُ مِنْ هَادٍةٌ وَمَنْ يَهْدِ اللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُ مِنْ مُّضِل [الزمر : ٣٦-٣٧]. وهذا من أسرار القضاء والقدر بحكم الأزل لا يُسْتَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْسَلُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٣] .
(And He did not compel) with a ḍamma on the yā and a kasra on the bā, meaning: He did not overpower any of His creation to disbelief nor to belief—and in another copy 'nor to belief'—and the meaning is that Allah does not create obedience and disobedience in the heart of the servant by way of compulsion and domination, but He creates them in his heart accompanied by the servant's choice and acquisition. For the one coerced to an action is he who, when he performs that action, dislikes it originally, and the one who chooses would prefer not to do it. Thus, the one under duress is like the believer if he is coerced to utter the word of disbelief and utters it outwardly while his heart is at peace with faith, and like the hypocrite who utters faith on the tongue while his heart is filled with disbelief. So the disbeliever is not excused in his disbelief, nor is the believer compelled in his faith. Rather, faith is beloved to the believers, just as disbelief is desired by the disbelievers. This is the meaning of His statement: 'Each party rejoices in what they have' [Muminun:53]. The ultimate matter is that Allah, by His grace, made faith beloved to us and adorned good deeds in our hearts, and made disbelief, immorality, and disobedience hateful to us. Praise be to Allah who guided us to this, and we would not have been guided had Allah not guided us. And by His justice, He withheld guidance from the people of disbelief and ingratitude, and made disobedience beloved to them and made faith hateful to them. So glory be to Him, glory be to Him. 'Allah leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills' [Muddaththir:31]. 'And whom Allah leads astray, for him there is no guide, and whom Allah guides, for him there is no misleader' [Zumar:36-37]. And this is among the secrets of divine decree and predestination by the eternal decree. 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned' [Anbiya:23].
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage explains the creedal article 'He did not compel anyone to disbelief or to faith.' The commentator clarifies that God does not create obedience and disobedience in the heart through compulsion (jabr), but rather creates them accompanied by the servant's choice and acquisition (kasb). He gives examples: the one forced to utter disbelief but whose heart is firm in faith is like the believer under duress; the hypocrite speaks faith while hearts are full of disbelief. Thus, the disbeliever is not excused, and the believer is not compelled. Faith is beloved to believers, disbelief desired by disbelievers, as the Quran says each party rejoices in its own way. The commentator then elaborates on divine grace and justice: God by His grace made faith beloved to believers and by His justice left the disbelievers without guidance and made disobedience beloved to them. He then cites several Quranic verses affirming God's absolute sovereignty in guidance and misguidance, concluding that these matters are among the secrets of divine decree (qaḍā' wa qadar) and that God is not questioned about what He does.

جبر
كسب
اختيار
إكراه
قضاء
قدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'not compelling' implies that humans create their own actions independently, without any divine creation.
Correction: The passage affirms that God creates all actions, but they are accompanied by the servant's choice and acquisition (kasb). So God is the creator, and the servant earns the action through free choice.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the relationship between God's creation of actions and the servant's choice?
A) God compels all actions without any choice.
B) The servant chooses independently without God's creation.
C) God creates the action but it is accompanied by the servant's choice and acquisition.
D) The servant creates his own actions entirely.

Key Takeaway
God does not compel anyone to disbelief or faith; He creates actions with the servant’s choice and acquisition, reconciling divine sovereignty with human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says that by His grace Allah made faith beloved to us and disbelief hateful. But do you find that in your daily choices, you sometimes prefer sin over obedience? Why? What does that reveal about the state of your heart? Will you honestly ask Allah to increase your love for faith and hatred for sin, starting today?
?
Consider the believer who was coerced to utter disbelief but remained steadfast in his heart. Have you ever been in a situation where you compromised your faith out of fear? How can the teaching that your inner conviction is what truly matters strengthen you to remain firm even under pressure? What step will you take this week to fortify your heart against such trials?
?
The lesson reminds us that we are not compelled in our faith—we choose and acquire it. Are you actively choosing faith every day, or have you become passive, relying only on your upbringing or environment? What specific action will you take today to consciously exercise your choice and acquisition of iman?

Divine Decree
beginner
6 min
God does not compel anyone to faith or disbelief
Explanation of no compulsion in faith and disbelief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God creates human actions in conjunction with the servant's free choice and acquisition, not by compulsion.

Core Idea
God creates actions with our choice, not by force.

One of the most delicate issues in Islamic theology is the relationship between divine creation of actions and human responsibility. This passage from al-Fiqh al-Akbar addresses that balance head-on. Before reading, note that the author is defending human accountability without denying God's role as the Creator of all acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Notice the linguistic clarification of the word 'ujbir' (compelled).
2
Distinguish jabr (compulsion) from kash (acquisition)
Understand the central claim: God does not create actions by brute force (jabr) but creates them together with the servant's choice (ikhtiyar) and acquisition (kash). This is the key to reconciling divine omnipotence and human responsibility.
3
Reflect on the two examples
Consider the examples of the believer forced to utter disbelief and the hypocrite who outwardly professes faith. Ask yourself: How do these examples illustrate the difference between compulsion and choice?
4
Connect to Quranic verses
The passage cites several verses about rejoicing in one's own ways, guidance, and misguidance. See how these verses support the idea that each person chooses their path, even though God ultimately guides or leads astray.
5
Synthesize the doctrine
Summarize in your own words: God creates all actions, but they are attributed to humans through their choice and acquisition. This preserves both God's sovereignty and human accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يُجبر أحدا من خلقه على الكفر وعلى الإيمان. ( ولم يُجبر) بضم الياء وكسر الباء، أي لم يقهر الله أحداً من خلقه على الكفر وعلى الإيمان) وفي نسخة ولا على الإيمان ، والمعنى أن الله تعالى لا يخلق الطاعة والمعصية في قلب العبد بطريق الجبر والغلبة، بل يخلقهما في قلبه مقرونا باختيار العبد وكسبه، فإن المكره على عمل هو الذي إذا عمل ذلك العمل يكرهه في الأصل، وكان المختار عنده أن لا يعمله فإنه عنده كالذليل كالمؤمن إذا أكره على إجراء كلمة الكفر فأجراها بظاهر البيان وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان، وكالمنافق حيث يجري الإيمان على اللسان وقلبه مشحون بالكفر، فليس الكافر في كفره معذوراً، ولا المؤمن في إيمانه مجبوراً، بل الإيمان محبوب للمؤمنين، كما أن الكفر مطلوب للكافرين، وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: كُلُّ حِزْبِ بِمَا لَدَيْهِمْ فَرِحُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون:٥٣]. غاية الأمر أن الله تعالى بفضله حبّب إلينا الإيمان وزيّن في قلوبنا الإحسان وكره إلينا الكفر والفسوق والعصيان والحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا وما كنا لنهتدي لولا أن هدانا الله، وبعدله ترك هداية أهل الكفر والكفران وحبّب إليهم العصيان وكره لديهم الإيمان، فسبحانه سبحانه، يُضِلُّ اللَّهُ مَنْ يَشَآءُ وَ يَهْدِى مَنْ يَشَاءُ [المدثر : ۳۱]، ﴿ وَمَن يُضْلِلِ اللَّهُ فَمَالَهُ مِنْ هَادٍةٌ وَمَنْ يَهْدِ اللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُ مِنْ مُّضِل [الزمر : ٣٦-٣٧]. وهذا من أسرار القضاء والقدر بحكم الأزل لا يُسْتَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْسَلُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٣] . (۱) الفردوس بمأثور الخطاب، ۱۸۷/۲، حدیث: ۲۹۳۷ ، وفيه بألفي عام قال ابن الجوزي: موضوع. الموضوعات، ٤٠١/١ .
And He did not compel anyone of His creation to disbelief or to faith. (And He did not compel) with dammah on the yā' and kasrah on the bā', meaning God did not overpower anyone of His creation to disbelief or to faith. And in another copy: 'nor to faith.' The meaning is that God the Exalted does not create obedience and disobedience in the heart of the servant by way of compulsion and overpowering, but He creates them in his heart accompanied by the servant's choice and acquisition (kash). For the one compelled to an action is he who, when he performs that action, dislikes it originally, and his choice would be not to do it. He is like the humiliated one, like the believer who is compelled to utter the word of disbelief and he utters it outwardly while his heart is at peace with faith, and like the hypocrite who utters faith on his tongue while his heart is filled with disbelief. So the disbeliever is not excused in his disbelief, nor is the believer compelled in his faith. Rather, faith is beloved to the believers, just as disbelief is desired by the disbelievers. And this is the meaning of His statement: 'Each party rejoices in what it has' [23:53]. Ultimately, God the Exalted, by His bounty, made faith beloved to us and adorned goodness in our hearts, and made disbelief, sin, and disobedience hateful to us. Praise be to God who guided us to this; we would not have been guided if God had not guided us. And by His justice, He left the guidance of the people of disbelief and ingratitude, and made disobedience beloved to them and faith hateful to them. So exalted is He, exalted is He. 'God leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills' [74:31]. 'Whoever God leads astray has no guide, and whoever God guides has no misleader' [39:36-37]. And this is among the secrets of divine decree and destiny by eternal decree; 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned' [21:23]. (1) Al-Firdaws bi Ma'thūr al-Khiṭāb, 2/187, Hadith 2937, and in it 'two thousand years'; Ibn al-Jawzī said: fabricated. Al-Mawḍū'āt, 1/401.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the doctrine that God does not compel anyone to faith or disbelief. The commentator begins by parsing the word 'ujbir' (compelled) linguistically, then clarifies the meaning: God does not create obedience or disobedience in the heart by brute force (jabr wa ghalaba) but creates them together with the servant's choice (ikhtiyar) and acquisition (kash). He illustrates with examples: a believer forced to utter disbelief outwardly while inwardly firm, and a hypocrite uttering faith outwardly while inwardly disbelieving. Thus the disbeliever is not excused for his disbelief, nor is the believer compelled in his faith; each acts according to his own inclination. The author then cites Quranic verses to show that each party rejoices in its own way, and that God by His grace makes faith beloved to believers and by His justice leaves disbelievers to their choice. He concludes with verses on guidance and misguidance, emphasizing that this is part of the secret of divine decree. The footnote mentions a hadith about the creation of souls but notes its fabrication by Ibn al-Jawzi.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage affirms that God creates actions, but He creates them together with the servant's choice and acquisition, not by compulsion. Thus, human actions are both created by God and earned by the servant.

A) God does not create any actions at all.

Key Takeaway
God creates all actions, but they are only validly attributed to humans through their free choice and acquisition, preserving both divine omnipotence and human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever blame your circumstances, upbringing, or even Allah for making you do it? The passage says Allah does not compel anyone to disbelief. Have you ever truly owned your sin as a choice you made, even if it felt difficult? Will you repent today with that full ownership?
?
The passage says Allah made faith beloved to the believers by His bounty. Do you feel that love for faith, or is your heart sometimes attracted to other things? If you find that you love something more than obedience, what does that say about your heart? Can you beg Allah to make faith more beloved to you than anything else?
?
The hypocrite says faith on his tongue but his heart is filled with disbelief. Is there any area of your life where your outward practice contradicts your inner state? Are you ever a hypocrite without realizing it? If you were tested today and forced to utter disbelief under threat, would your heart remain firm or would it waver? Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
God Creates Humans Neutral; Faith and Disbelief Are Their Choice
The author denies compulsion in faith/disbelief, affirms human choice, and clarifies divine knowledge and attributes are unchanging.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic theology affirms that God creates humans with the capacity for faith or disbelief, and that His knowledge and attributes remain unchanged by human actions.

Core Idea
God's knowledge does not change, but the objects of His knowledge do.

This passage from al-Fiqh al-Akbar tackles a delicate balance: God's sovereignty versus human responsibility. The author affirms that God creates humans as neutral persons, capable of both faith and disbelief. Then he explains how divine foreknowledge and eternal attributes relate to human choices without implying change in God.

Guided Path
1
Understand the denial of compulsion
Read the opening sentence: 'And He did not create them as believers or disbelievers — i.e., by compulsion and force.' Note that the author immediately clarifies that God's creation does not predetermine faith or disbelief.
This counters the misconception that God forces belief or disbelief.
2
Grasp the concept of 'ashkhas'
The author says God created them as 'ashkhas' (persons), meaning capable of accepting or rejecting faith. This establishes human capacity and choice.
The term 'ashkhas' is key: it signifies a neutral state with potential.
3
Examine divine knowledge and attributes
The passage then explains that God knows the disbeliever as a disbeliever and the believer as a believer, but His knowledge and eternal attributes (wrath, pleasure) do not change. Only the objects (muta'alliqāt) change with time.
This part guards against the idea that God's attributes change due to human actions.
4
Reflect on the role of actual deeds
Finally, the author states that God's foreknowledge does not negate the need for the servant's actual choice and deed; accountability is based on manifested actions.
This shows that divine omniscience and human responsibility coexist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا خلقهم مؤمنا ولا كافرا أي بالجبر والإكراه ولكن خلقهم أشخاصا أي قابلة لقبول الإيمان إخلاصا، ولاختيار الكفر على توهم كونه لهم خلاصا. والإيمان والكفر فعل العباد أي بحسب اختيارهم لا على وجه اضطرارهم. وسبحان من أقام العباد فيما أراد. يعلم الله تعالى من يكفر في حال كفره كافراً أي وأبغضه كما في نسخة. فإذا آمن بعد ذلك أي بعد ارتكاب كفره علمه مؤمنا في حال إيمانه أي وأحبّه كما في نسخة. من غير أن يتغيّر علمه أي بتغير كفر عبده وإيمانه، ولا صفته أي ومن غير أن يتغير نعته الأزلي من الغضب والرضاء المتعلقين بالكفر والإيمان، وإنما التغيير في متعلقهما باختلاف الزمان. بل وقد علم بإيمان بعض وكفر آخرين قبل وجودهم في عالم شهودهم إلا أنه سبحانه وكرمه لا يعمل بمجرد تعلق علمه بل لابد من إظهار اختيار العبد وحصول عمله ليترتب عليه الحساب ويتفرع عليه الثواب أو العقاب. والله أعلم بالصواب.
And He did not create them as believers or disbelievers — i.e., by compulsion and force — but He created them as persons, i.e., capable of accepting faith sincerely and of choosing disbelief upon the delusion that it is their salvation. And faith and disbelief are the act of the servants, i.e., according to their choice, not by way of coercion. Glory be to Him who established the servants in what He willed. God knows the one who disbelieves, in the state of his disbelief, as a disbeliever — i.e., and He hates him, as in a copy. Then if he believes after that, i.e., after committing his disbelief, He knows him as a believer in the state of his faith — i.e., and He loves him, as in a copy. Without His knowledge changing, i.e., due to the change of his servant's disbelief and faith, nor His attribute, i.e., without His eternal attribute of wrath and pleasure pertaining to disbelief and faith changing. Rather, the change is only in their objects (muta'alliqāt) according to the difference of time. Indeed, He knew the faith of some and the disbelief of others before their existence in the world of their witness. However, He, exalted and generous, does not act solely by the attachment of His knowledge; rather, the manifestation of the servant's choice and the occurrence of his deed are necessary so that accountability may be based upon it and reward or punishment may branch from it. And God knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage explains the second article: God did not create humans as believers or disbelievers by compulsion, but as neutral persons (ashkhas) capable of accepting faith or choosing disbelief. Faith and disbelief are the servants' own acts according to their choice, not by coercion. The author then discusses divine knowledge: God knows the disbeliever as a disbeliever and hates him, and knows the believer as a believer and loves him. However, neither God's knowledge nor His eternal attributes (such as wrath and pleasure) change when the servant changes; rather, only the objects (muta'alliqāt) of those attributes change with time. God already knew the faith or disbelief of each person before their existence. Yet, He does not base reward or punishment solely on His foreknowledge; rather, He requires the actual manifestation of the servant's choice and deed so that accountability is meaningful. The passage emphasizes both divine sovereignty and human responsibility.

Key Terms
خلقهم أشخاصا
فعل العباد
يعلم الله
التغيير في المتعلق
الغضب
الرضاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's knowledge or attributes change when a person changes from disbelief to faith.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that God's knowledge and eternal attributes (wrath and pleasure) do not change; only the objects of these attributes change with time.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about change in God's attributes when a servant changes from disbelief to faith?
A) God's attribute of wrath changes to pleasure.
B) God's knowledge changes from knowing him as a disbeliever to knowing him as a believer.
C) God's eternal attributes of wrath and pleasure do not change; only their objects change with time.
D) God's attributes remain the same but His knowledge changes.

Key Takeaway
God creates humans with capacity for choice; His knowledge and attributes are unchanging, and accountability requires the actual deed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think of a sin you keep falling into. Do you ever internally blame Qadar or say 'God made me do it'? How does this lesson's insistence on your own choice confront that excuse, and what will you change?
?
God's wrath is attached to disbelief — not just past disbelief but any persistent disbelief in your heart. Is there an area where you are comfortable with unbelief (e.g., doubts, neglect of obligations)? Will you turn from it now to become an object of His pleasure?

All actions of servants are their acquisition in reality
The author affirms that all human actions are truly acquired by the servant, refuting Mu'tazilite and Jabrite extremes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition (kash) and how it distinguishes human responsibility from divine creation while refuting the extremes of Mu'tazilites and Jabrites.

Core Idea
Human actions are truly acquired by choice, not created by the servant nor devoid of choice.

This passage from the Ash'ari tradition presents the middle path on human actions: they are not created by us (as Mu'tazilites claim) nor are we forced without choice (as Jabrites claim). Instead, Allah creates the action and we acquire it, making us truly responsible. Let's read the original text and unpack its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the refutation of two groups.
2
Identify the core claim
The passage states that all actions of servants are acquisition (kash) in reality, not metaphorically or by coercion. Find the key phrase and note what it affirms and negates.
3
Understand the refutations
The passage refutes the Mu'tazilites, who say the servant creates actions, and the Jabrites, who negate acquisition and choice entirely. Compare these positions with the Ash'ari middle path.
Reflect on why both extremes are problematic.
4
Connect to the Quranic principle
The passage cites the verse 'For it (the soul) is what it has acquired and against it is what it has earned.' Consider how this verse supports the Ash'ari view.
This verse is from Surah Al-Baqarah, verse 286.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجميع أفعال العباد من الحركة والسكون أي على أي وجه يكون الكفر والإيمان والطاعة والعصيان كسبهم على الحقيقة أي لا على طريق المجاز في النسبة، ولا على سبيل الإكراه والغلبة، بل باختيارهم في فعلهم بحسب اختلاف أهواءهم وميل أنفسهم، فلها ما كسبت وعليها ما اكتسبت لا كما زعمت المعتزلة، أن العبد خالق لأفعاله الاختيارية، الضرب والشتم وغير ذلك، ولا كما زعمت الجبرية القائلون بنفي الكسب والاختيار بالكلية من
And all the actions of the servants, from movement and stillness, in whatever form they take, whether disbelief and faith or obedience and disobedience, are their acquisition (kash) in reality — i.e., not in a metaphorical sense of attribution, nor by way of coercion and overpowering, but by their choice in their action according to the difference of their whims and inclination of their souls. So for it (the soul) is what it has acquired and against it is what it has earned. Not as the Mu'tazilites claimed that the servant is the creator of his voluntary actions, such as hitting and insulting and other than that, nor as the Jabrites claimed who completely negate acquisition and choice.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage defines the Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition (kash). It states that all human actions, including physical movements and states, whether they be disbelief, faith, obedience, or disobedience, are truly the servant's acquisition — not in a metaphorical sense, nor by coercion. The servant performs them by his own choice according to his whims and inclinations. The Quranic principle 'to it what it has acquired and against it what it has earned' is invoked. The passage then refutes two opposing extremes: the Mu'tazilites, who say the servant is the creator of his voluntary actions (thus denying God's role), and the Jabrites, who completely negate acquisition and choice (thus denying human responsibility). The Ash'ari position maintains that God creates the actions while the servant acquires them, preserving both divine omnipotence and human accountability.

المعتزلة

الاختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Acquisition means the servant creates his own actions.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that actions are acquisition in reality, not creation. The servant chooses and acquires, but Allah creates the action.

Checkpoint

A) The Ash'arites and the Maturidis.
B) The Mu'tazilites and the Jabrites.
C) The Qadaris and the Jahmis.
D) The Sunnis and the Shia.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition affirms that human actions are truly our own by choice, while Allah is the sole creator of all actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Which extreme have you unconsciously leaned towards—thinking you are the sole creator of your deeds (like the Mu'tazilites) or feeling hopelessly compelled (like the Jabrites)? What concrete step will you take today to embrace the Ash'ari middle path in your daily choices?

Human Actions Are Acquired, Not Created
Explanation that Allah creates persons, not belief states

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that while Allah creates human persons, He does not create their faith or disbelief; rather, these are the servants' own actions acquired through choice.

Core Idea
Allah creates persons, not their beliefs; faith and disbelief are human acts.

This passage from the commentary on Fiqh al-Akbar clarifies a key point about divine predestination and human responsibility. The author explains that Allah creates human beings as individuals with capacity, but their faith or unbelief is their own doing, not a direct creation by compulsion. This establishes the doctrine of kasb (acquisition).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on creation and acquisition
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Notice how the author first negates that Allah creates believers/disbelievers by compulsion, then affirms that He creates them as persons with capacity.
The passage uses 'ولا... ولكن' structure.
2
Understand the khalq vs kasb distinction
Identify that 'خلق' (creation) applies to persons, while 'إيمان' and 'كفر' are 'فعل العباد' (acts of servants). This is the core distinction.
3
Note the emphasis on choice
Observe the phrase 'بحسب اختيارهم لا على وجه اضطرارهم' – by their choice, not compulsion. This refutes fatalism.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why this distinction matters for justice and human responsibility. The passage implies that reward and punishment are only meaningful if actions are freely chosen.
This connects to the broader Islamic doctrine of kasb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا خلقهم مؤمنا ولا كافرا، ولكن خلقهم أشخاصاً، والإيمان والكفر فعل العباد، يعلم الله تعالى من يكفر في حال كفره كافراً، فإذا آمن بعد ذلك علمه مؤمناً في حال إيمانه من غير أن يتغير علمه وصفته، (ولا) خلقهم مؤمنا ولا (كافرا أى بالجبر والإكراه ولكن خلقهم أشخاصا أي قابلة لقبول الإيمان إخلاصا، ولاختيار الكفر على توهم كونه لهم خلاصا والإيمان والكفر فعل العباد أي بحسب اختيارهم لا على وجه اضطرارهم وسبحان من أقام العباد فيما أراد، (يعلم الله تعالى من يكفر في حال كفره كافراً أي وأبغضه كما في نسخة (فإذا آمن بعد ذلك أي ارتكاب كفره علمه مؤمنا في حال إيمانه أي ،وأحبّه كما في نسخة (من غير أن يتغيّر علمه أي بتغير كفر عبده وإيمانه (وصفته) أي ومن غير أن يتغير نعته الأزلي الأزلي من الغضب والرضاء المتعلقين بالكفر والإيمان، وإنما التغيير في متعلقهما باختلاف الزمان، بل وقد علم بإيمان بعض وكفر آخرين قبل وجودهم في عالم شهودهم إلا أنه سبحانه وكرمه لا يعمل بمجرد تعلق علمه بل لابد من إظهار اختيار العبد وحصول عمله ليترتب عليه الحساب ويتفرع عليه الثواب أو العقاب، والله أعلم بالصواب.
And He did not create them as believers or disbelievers, but He created them as persons, and faith and unbelief are the act of the servants. Allah, may He be exalted, knows the one who disbelieves, in the state of his disbelief, as a disbeliever. Then if he believes after that, He knows him as a believer in the state of his belief, without His knowledge and attribute changing. (And He did not) create them as believers nor (disbelievers) – meaning by compulsion and coercion, but He created them as persons, meaning capable of accepting faith sincerely, and of choosing disbelief under the illusion that it would be their salvation. And faith and disbelief are the act of the servants – meaning according to their choice, not by way of compulsion. And glory be to Him who established the servants in what He willed. (Allah, may He be exalted, knows) the one who disbelieves, in the state of his disbelief, as a disbeliever – meaning and He hates him, as in one copy. (Then if he believes after that) – i.e., after committing his disbelief – He knows him as a believer in the state of his belief – meaning and He loves him, as in one copy. (Without His knowledge changing) – i.e., due to the change of his servant's disbelief and belief – (and His attribute) – i.e., and without His eternal description changing, of anger and pleasure connected to disbelief and faith. Rather, the change is in their objects according to difference in time. Moreover, He has known the faith of some and the disbelief of others before their existence in the world of their witnessing. However, He, glorified and generous, does not act merely according to His knowledge's connection, but there must be a manifestation of the servant's choice and the occurrence of his action, so that reckoning may follow and reward or punishment may branch from it. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn of Fiqh al-Akbar. It explains that Allah does not create human beings as believers or disbelievers by compulsion; rather, He creates them as persons capable of choice. Faith and disbelief are actions of the servants themselves, performed by their own choice, not by coercion. The passage then addresses divine knowledge: Allah knows the disbeliever as a disbeliever while he is in that state, and if he later believes, He knows him as a believer. This does not imply a change in Allah's knowledge or attributes; rather, the change occurs only in the objects of knowledge (i.e., the states of the servant). The author emphasizes that Allah's eternal attributes of anger and pleasure are related to disbelief and belief, but these attributes do not change—only their objects change with time. Furthermore, Allah already knows the faith of some and the disbelief of others before they exist, but He does not punish or reward based solely on that knowledge; He waits until the servant manifests his choice and performs the action, so that reckoning and reward or punishment are justly applied.

كسب (kasb)
إيمان (iman)
كفر (kufr)

Correction: The passage teaches that Allah creates the person, but faith and disbelief are the servant's own acquired acts, done by choice, not by divine creation of those specific states.

Divine Knowledge Unchanging Despite Human Change
Explanation of the unchanging nature of divine knowledge and attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's knowledge of a person's belief or disbelief does not change over time, and that His attributes remain eternal while only the objects of His knowledge change.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge is eternal; changes in human states do not alter His essence.

This passage continues the commentary by addressing a nuanced point: if Allah knows the disbeliever as a disbeliever, does that mean His knowledge changes when the person later believes? The author clarifies that Allah's knowledge and attributes are unchanging. The change is only in the objects of His knowledge—the states of the servant. This preserves divine perfection and upholds justice, as Allah waits for the servant's choice to manifest before rewarding or punishing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divine knowledge
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the examples: Allah knows the disbeliever in his disbelief, and if he later believes, He knows him as a believer.
Focus on the phrase 'من غير أن يتغير علمه وصفته'.
2
Understand that change is in the object, not subject
The passage explicitly says that Allah's knowledge and attribute do not change. The change is only in the servant's states (disbelief to belief), which are the objects of knowledge.
3
Note the role of manifestation of choice
The passage ends by stating that Allah does not act solely on His prior knowledge; He waits for the servant to manifest his choice and perform the action, so that reckoning is just.
This means divine foreknowledge does not negate human responsibility.
4
Reflect on the attributes of anger and pleasure
The passage mentions that Allah's attributes of anger and pleasure are eternal and do not change; only their objects change based on the servant's state.
This is a deeper point about divine attributes.

Actions Are Acquisition: The Sunni Middle Path
Affirmation of kasb and refutation of Mu'tazila and Jabariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of kasb (acquisition) in Sunni theology and how it differs from the Mu'tazili and Jabari positions.

Core Idea
Human actions are truly acquired by choice, yet created by Allah.

This lesson explores a central point of Sunni creed: how human actions relate to divine power. The author clarifies that every action of a servant is truly acquired (kasb) through their own choice, neither coerced nor independently created. This middle path refutes both the Mu'tazila, who claim humans create their own actions, and the Jabariyya, who deny human choice entirely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the overall meaning. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the key terms and sects
Look for the terms kasb, ikhtiyar, Mu'tazila, and Jabariyya. Understand what each refers to.
Kasb is the central concept; the other terms help define it by contrast.
3
Examine the refutation of extremes
Pay attention to how the passage rejects two opposing views: the Mu'tazili claim that humans create their actions, and the Jabari claim that humans have no real choice.
These refutations clarify the Sunni position.
4
Reflect on the Quranic echo
The phrase 'So for it is what it acquired...' is from the Quran. Consider how this verse supports the concept of moral responsibility within divine creation.
This ties kasb to accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجميع أفعال العباد من الحركة والسكون أي على أي وجه يكون الكفر والإيمان والطاعة والعصيان كسبهم على الحقيقة أي لا على طريق المجاز في النسبة، ولا على سبيل الإكراه والغلبة، بل باختيارهم في فعلهم بحسب اختلاف أهواءهم وميل أنفسهم، فلها ما كسبت وعليها ما اكتسبت لا كما زعمت المعتزلة، أن العبد خالق لأفعاله الاختيارية، الضرب والشتم وغير ذلك، ولا كما زعمت الجبرية القائلون بنفي الكسب والاختيار بالكلية
And all the actions of the servants, whether movement or stillness, whatever kind they are – disbelief, faith, obedience, or disobedience – are their acquisition (kasb) in reality, i.e., not metaphorically in attribution, nor by way of coercion and domination, but by their choice in their action according to the difference of their desires and the inclination of their souls. So for it (the soul) is what it acquired, and against it is what it earned, not as the Mu'tazila claimed that the servant is the creator of his voluntary actions, such as hitting, insulting, and so on, nor as the Jabariyya claimed, who deny acquisition (kasb) and choice entirely.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage defines kasb (acquisition) and contrasts it with Mu'tazili and Jabari positions. The commentary explains that all human actions – whether movement or stillness, and whether they are disbelief, faith, obedience, or disobedience – are kasb 'ala al-haqiqah (truly acquisition). This means the attribution of actions to the servant is not metaphorical; the actions are truly his in the sense that he performs them by his own choice and power, but not independently of Allah's creation. The phrase 'so for it is what it acquired and against it is what it earned' echoes Quranic language, indicating moral responsibility. The passage then explicitly refutes two extremes: the Mu'tazila, who claim the servant creates his own actions (thus making the servant independent of Allah), and the Jabariyya, who deny any real acquisition or choice from the servant (thus making the servant a mere puppet). The middle path of Ahl al-Sunna is that actions are created by Allah but acquired by the servant through his choice.

Key Terms
كسب (kasb)
اختيار (ikhtiyar)
معتزلة (Mu'tazila)
جبرية (Jabariyya)
خلق (khalq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think kasb means the servant creates the action alongside Allah.
Correction: Kasb is not creation; it is acquisition through choice, while creation is solely Allah's.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the Mu'tazila and Jabariyya positions?
A) Both are correct in different ways
B) The Mu'tazila deny the servant's choice, and the Jabariyya affirm the servant creates his actions
C) The Mu'tazila claim the servant creates his actions, and the Jabariyya deny acquisition and choice entirely
D) The passage does not mention either group

Key Takeaway
Human actions are truly acquired by the servant through choice, but ultimately created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you tend to blame your circumstances or Allah's decree? How does this lesson's affirmation of your own acquisition of actions (kasb) confront that tendency? What specific step will you take today to own your actions as your choices, while still attributing their creation to Allah?
?
The Mu'tazila claim you create your actions. The Jabariyya deny your choice. In your daily life, which extreme do you lean toward more: overestimating your independence or underestimating your responsibility? How does the Sunni middle path (kasb) call you to change one habit this week?

Quranic Proofs That Allah Creates All Actions
Three Quranic proofs for Allah's creatorship of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three Quranic proofs that Allah is the Creator of all human actions, and why this refutes the Mu'tazilite position.

Core Idea
Allah's creation encompasses every action—no servant creates independently.

The passage begins by affirming that Allah is the Creator of all actions. It then marshals three decisive Quranic proofs that establish Allah's sole creatorship. These verses not only define the boundaries of divine power but also serve as the foundation for the doctrine of kasb (acquisition). The first two verses establish the universal scope of creation, while the third directly links Allah's creation to human actions, as used by Imam Abu Hanifa in debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation to understand the meaning of each verse and its interpretation.
Notice how each verse is introduced with 'لقوله تعالى'.
2
Identify the three Quranic proofs
Locate the verses: 39:62, 16:17, and 37:96. For each, note what specific aspect of creatorship it demonstrates.
The commentary explains the reasoning behind each verse.
3
Understand the refutation of Mu'tazila
These verses collectively refute the idea that servants create their own actions. See how each verse denies independent creatorship.
The Mu'tazila claimed that actions proceed from human power alone.
4
Reflect on the historical debate
Imam Abu Hanifa used verse 37:96 to argue against Amr ibn Ubayd, a leading Mu'tazili. This shows the practical application of these proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والله تعالى خالقها أي موجد أفعال العباد وفق ما أراد لقوله تعالى: { اللَّهُ خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْء } [الزمر: 62]، أي ممكن بدلالة العقل، وفعل العبد شيء ولقوله تعالى: { أَفَمَنْ يَخْلُقُ كَمَنْ لا يَخْلُقُ } [النحل: 17]، أي الذي يصدر منه حقيقة الخلق ليس كمن لا يصدر منه ذلك في شيء، وهذا في مقام التمدح بالخالقية وكونها سببا لاستحقاق العبادة. ولقوله تعالى: { وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ } [الصافات: 96]، أي وعملكم أو معمولكم، وبه احتج أبو حنيفة رحمه الله على عمرو بن عبيد. وفي حديث رواه الحاكم وصححه البيهقي من حديث حذيفة مرفوعاً: ((إن الله صانع كلَّ صانع وصنعته)) . ولذا وبخهم سبحانه بقوله تعالى: { أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ } [الصافات: 95] أي ما تعملون من الأصنام، وبقوله تعالى: { أَفَمَنْ يَخْلُقُ كَمَنْ لَا يَخْلُقُ } [النحل:17]، ولأن العبد لو كان خالقاً لأفعاله لكان عالماً بتفاصيلها كما يشير إليه سبحانه بقوله: { أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ } [الملك: 14]، وقول علي كرم الله تعالى وجهه: عرفت الله بفسخ العزائم، ولقد أغرب المعتزلة
And Allah, may He be exalted, is their Creator – i.e., the originator of the actions of the servants according to what He willed, due to His saying: { Allah is the Creator of everything } [az-Zumar: 62] – i.e., everything possible by indication of reason, and the action of the servant is a thing – and due to His saying: { Is He who creates like he who does not create? } [an-Nahl: 17] – i.e., the one from whom the reality of creation issues is not like the one from whom that does not issue in anything, and this is in the context of praising oneself with creatorship and its being a cause for deserving worship. And due to His saying: { And Allah created you and what you do } [as-Saffat: 96] – i.e., your action or your made thing, and with it Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, argued against Amr ibn Ubayd. And in a hadith narrated by al-Hakim and authenticated by al-Bayhaqi from the hadith of Hudhayfa, marfu': 'Indeed Allah is the Maker of every maker and his handiwork.' Therefore, He, glorified, rebuked them with His saying: { Do you worship what you carve? } [as-Saffat: 95] – i.e., what you make of idols – and with His saying: { Is He who creates like he who does not create? } [an-Nahl: 17], and because if the servant were the creator of his actions, he would be knowledgeable of their details, as He, glorified, indicates by His saying: { Should He not know who created? } [al-Mulk: 14], and the saying of Ali, may Allah honor his face: 'I knew Allah by the annulment of determinations.' And indeed the Mu'tazila went to extremes.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural and rational proofs that Allah is the Creator of all human actions. It begins by stating 'Allah is their Creator' – referring to the actions previously discussed. The first proof is the Quranic verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' (az-Zumar 62), which is general and includes human actions. The commentary notes that 'everything' here means every possible thing, and the servant's action is a possible thing. The second proof is the rhetorical question 'Is He who creates like he who does not create?' (an-Nahl 17), which establishes that true creation belongs only to Allah. The third proof is 'Allah created you and what you do' (as-Saffat 96), which is interpreted as 'your action' or 'the thing you make'. The author mentions that Imam Abu Hanifa used this verse to argue against the Mu'tazili scholar Amr ibn Ubayd. A hadith is also cited: 'Indeed Allah is the Maker of every maker and his handiwork,' reported by al-Hakim and authenticated by al-Bayhaqi. This shows that even the maker and his making are created by Allah. Then the passage presents a rational proof: if the servant were the creator of his actions, he would have complete knowledge of all their details, but humans are often unaware of the full reality of their actions. This is supported by the verse 'Should He not know who created?' (al-Mulk 14) and the saying of Ali: 'I knew Allah by the annulment of determinations' – meaning that when one resolves to do something and it is not carried out as intended, that shows a higher power overrides human will. The passage concludes that the Mu'tazila went astray by claiming the servant creates his own actions.

Key Terms
خالق
فعل
خلق
ممكن
عمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The servant creates his own actions independently.
Correction: Allah is the Creator of everything, including the servant's actions, as proven by Quranic verses.

Checkpoint
Which verse did Abu Hanifa use to argue against Amr ibn Ubayd?
A) Quran 39:62
B) Quran 16:17
C) Quran 37:96
D) Quran 37:95

Key Takeaway
The Quran unequivocally establishes that Allah is the Creator of all actions, leaving no room for independent creatorship of servants.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah creates even your most private thoughts and intentions, how does that affect the way you guard your heart? Will you still say 'I can't help thinking that way' knowing those thoughts are created by Allah and you bear responsibility?
?
The verse 'Is He who creates like he who does not create?' (16:17) is meant to humble you before the Creator. When you perform a good deed, do you secretly feel pride as if you originated it? How will you now redirect that feeling into thankfulness to the One who actually created that action?
?
Abu Hanifa used the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' to correct a misguided scholar. If you encounter someone today who says 'I am the sole author of my destiny', will you have the courage and knowledge to gently correct them with this very verse? What would you actually say, and what keeps you from saying it?

Hadith and Rational Proof for Allah's Creation of Actions
Hadith and rational proof for Allah's creatorship of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith and rational arguments proving that Allah creates all actions, and why the Mu'tazila are mistaken.

Core Idea
Even the maker and his handiwork are created by Allah, and the servant's lack of perfect knowledge disproves his creatorship.

The passage continues with a powerful hadith that explicitly states Allah is the Maker of every maker. It then reinforces the Quranic proofs with a rational argument: if the servant truly created his actions, he would know them perfectly, but he does not. This is supported by Imam Ali's insight about the annulment of determinations.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and understand its implication
Read the hadith: 'Indeed Allah is the Maker of every maker and his handiwork.' Reflect on how this shows that even the act of making is created by Allah.
The hadith is narrated by al-Hakim and authenticated by al-Bayhaqi.
2
Follow the rational proof
The passage argues: if the servant were creator, he would know his creation fully, but he does not (as shown by Quran 67:14). Therefore, he cannot be the creator.
This is a qiyas argument: a creator knows his creation, but the servant lacks perfect knowledge, so he is not the creator.
3
Examine Imam Ali's saying
Imam Ali said: 'I knew Allah by the annulment of determinations.' Understand how this illustrates that human resolutions are overridden by Allah's will.
When a person intends something and it doesn't happen, that shows a higher power is at work.
4
Reflect on the conclusion about Mu'tazila
The passage ends by stating that the Mu'tazila went to extremes (أغربوا) in their view. Consider how all the proofs together refute their position.

Refuting the Mu'tazila on Divine Creation of Actions
The commentator refutes a Mu'tazila objection and clarifies the meaning of 'khalq' in Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars refute the Mu'tazila claim that if God creates all actions, He would be attributed with sinful acts, and how the term 'khalq' is properly understood when applied to humans.

Core Idea
God creates actions, but the description belongs to the creature in whom the action subsists.

The Mu'tazila objected that if God creates all human actions, then He would be responsible for sins. This lesson examines the refutation based on the distinction between creation (ījād) and subsistence (qiyām). It also clarifies the meaning of 'creation' when attributed to humans in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila objection
Start by reading the passage to see the exact objection: if God creates actions, He would be the doer of sinful acts like standing, sitting, theft, and adultery.
The objection is stated at the beginning.
2
Understand the core distinction
Focus on the commentator's key principle: the one described by an action is the one in whom it subsists, not the one who brings it into existence. This refutes the objection without denying God's creative power.
This distinction is central to Sunni theology on human action.
3
Examine the Quranic verses
Notice how the commentator addresses verses that use 'khalq' for humans (plural form in 23:14 and attributed to Jesus in 5:110). He explains that 'khalq' here means determination and shaping, not bringing into existence from nothing.
The term 'khalq' has different meanings in different contexts.
4
Reflect on divine transcendence
Consider how this interpretation preserves God's transcendence: He creates but is not described by the actions that subsist in creatures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قول المعتزلة : «لو كان الله خالقا لأفعال العباد لكان هو القائم والقاعد والأكل والشارب والزاني والسارق». وهذا جهل عظيم، فمدفوع بأن المتصف بالشيء من قام به ذلك الشيء لا من أوجده إذ لا يرون أن الله تعالى هو الخالق للسواد والبياض وسائر الصفات في الأجسام، فالإيجاد هو فعل الله والموجود وهو الحركة فعل العبد، وهو موصوف به حتى يشتق له منه اسم المتحرك، ولا يتصف الله بذلك، وأما قوله تعالى: فَتَبَرَكَ اللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخُلِقِينَ [المؤمنون:١٤]، بصيغة الجمع، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ تَخْلُقُ مِنَ الطِّينِ﴾ [المائدة:١١٠]، بإضافة الخلق إلى عيسى فجوابه أن الخلق هاهنا بمعنى التقدير والتصوير، فإن العبد بقدر طاقة البشرية له بعض التدبير إن وافق التقدير.
And as for the statement of the Mu'tazila: 'If God were the creator of the actions of the slaves, then He would be the one standing, sitting, eating, drinking, fornicating, and stealing.' This is great ignorance, and it is rebutted by the fact that the one described by something is the one in whom that thing subsists, not the one who brings it into existence, since they do not see that God is the creator of blackness and whiteness and all attributes in bodies. So bringing into existence is the act of God, and the existing thing, which is the movement, is the act of the slave, and the slave is described by it such that the name 'mover' is derived for him from it, and God is not described by that. And as for His saying: 'So blessed is Allah, the best of creators' [23:14] in the plural form, and His saying: 'And when you create from clay' [5:110] attributing creation to Jesus, the reply is that 'creation' here means determination and formation, for the slave, to the extent of human capacity, has some planning if it coincides with divine decree.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (shubha wa jawab). The Mu'tazila object: if God creates all human actions, then He would be directly attributed with sinful acts like standing, sitting, theft, and adultery. The commentator refutes this by distinguishing between the one who creates an action (mūjid) and the one in whom the action subsists (al-qā'im bihi). The action subsists in the slave; thus the slave is described as 'mover', etc., not God. God creates the action as an existing entity (ījād), but the action's locus is the slave. Regarding the Quranic verses that use the word 'khāliqīn' (creators) plural and attribute 'khalq' to Jesus, the commentator explains that 'khalq' here means 'taqdīr' (determination) and 'taswīr' (shaping). Human 'creation' is only planning and shaping within the limits of human capacity, which only becomes effective if it conforms to God's decree.

Key Terms
خالق
إيجاد
موجود
تخليق
تقدير
تصوير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates an act, He becomes directly responsible for it and is described by it.
Correction: God creates the act as an existing entity (ījād), but the act subsists in the creature. Therefore, the creature is described by the act, not God.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is God not described by the actions He creates in humans?
A) Because God does not create those actions
B) Because the action subsists in the slave, not in God
C) Because God only creates good actions
D) Because the slave creates the action independently

Key Takeaway
God creates all actions, but the creature is described by the action because the action subsists in the creature, preserving God's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action you perform, even your sins, is created by Allah? If so, how does that affect your view of your own responsibility and your need for His mercy? Will you repent more sincerely knowing your action is created but you are the one described by it?
?
When you plan your future, do you rely on your own 'creation' (planning) or do you recognize that your planning only becomes reality if it coincides with Allah's decree? Will you start your next plan by saying 'insha’Allah' with genuine reliance on Him?
?
The Mu'tazila feared that attributing all actions to God would make Him responsible for evil. Are you willing to submit to the truth that Allah creates all actions, even those that seem evil, while affirming His perfect justice and wisdom? What changes in your heart when you accept this?

Ibn al-Humam on Divine Power and Human Agency
Ibn al-Humam argues for the independence of human voluntary action from direct divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn al-Humam's logical argument that if God gives power to the slave, it must have a real effect, and the impossibility of two independent agents necessitates that human voluntary actions are created by the slave, not directly by God.

Core Idea
If power has effect, two agents cannot act on one effect, so voluntary acts must be from the slave.

This passage presents a pivotal argument from Ibn al-Humam that challenges the Asharite concept of kasb by highlighting a logical tension: if God creates power in humans, that power must produce its own effect. But if God also creates that effect, we have two independent agents for one effect—impossible. This leads to the Mu'tazila conclusion that humans independently create their own actions. Understanding this argument is crucial for grasping the debate on divine omnipotence and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'fa-inna' and 'fa-wajaba'.
The passage is a single continuous argument by Ibn al-Humam.
2
Identify the key premises
Find the premises: God creates power in the slave; power is only for effect; two independent effectors cannot produce one effect.
These premises are given as statements or implied.
3
Trace the conclusion
See how the premises lead to the conclusion: the general texts must be specified to exclude voluntary actions, so humans independently create their own actions.
The conclusion is presented as necessary ('fawajaba').
4
Reflect on the consequence
Note the consequence: if not, it would be pure compulsion (jabr), nullifying command and prohibition.
This shows the stakes of the argument.
5
Consider the dialectical context
Realize this is presented as a potential objection or proof; the commentator may later refute it. For now, grasp the logic.
Ibn al-Humam is known for his critical approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن تحقيق المرام ما ذكره ابن الهمام في هذا المقام حيث قال: فإن قيل: لا شك أنه تعالى خلق للعبد قدرة على الأفعال، ولذا ندرك تفرقة بين الحركة المقدورة وهي الاختيارية وبين الرعدة الضرورية، والقدرة ليست خاصيتها إلا التأثير، أي إيجاد المقدور، فإن القدرة صفة تؤثر على وفق الإرادة. ويستحيل اجتماع مؤثرين مستقلين على أثر واحد، فوجب تخصيص عمومات النصوص السابقة بما سوى أفعال العباد الاختيارية، فيكونون مستقلين بإيجاد أفعالهم الاختيارية الحادثة بخلق الله تعالى، كما هو رأي المعتزلة، وإلا كان جبرا محضا فيبطل الأمر والنهى. بقدرتهم
Then know that the verification of the desired point is what Ibn al-Humam mentioned in this context, where he said: If it is said: There is no doubt that He, exalted, created for the slave a power over actions, and therefore we perceive a difference between the voluntary movement (al-mutaharrikah al-muqaddarah) which is optional, and the involuntary tremor (al-ra'dah al-daruriyyah). And power has no property except effect, i.e., bringing into existence the object of power. For power is an attribute that effects in accordance with will. And it is impossible for two independent effectors to come together on one effect. So it is necessary to specify the general texts (previous) to exclude the voluntary actions of the slaves, so that they are independent in bringing into existence their voluntary actions that come into existence by the creation of Allah, as is the view of the Mu'tazila. Otherwise, it would be pure compulsion (jabr) and would nullify command and prohibition. By their power.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn al-Humam's 'tahqīq' (verification) of the issue. He sets up a hypothetical objection: if God creates power in the slave, we can distinguish between voluntary movements (powered) and involuntary tremors (unpowered). Power's nature is to produce an effect (ījād al-maqdūr). If God also creates the effect, then two independent agents (God and the slave) would produce the same effect, which is impossible. Therefore, the general Quranic verses that ascribe all creation to God (like 'Allah is the creator of all things') must be interpreted as excluding voluntary human actions, so that the slave independently produces his own actions (by the power God created). This is the Mu'tazila view. If we deny that, we end up with pure compulsion (jabr), which negates the validity of divine commands and prohibitions. The passage thus presents a proof for human acquisition (kasb) as understood by the Asharites, but it reproduces the Mu'tazila argument for independence; the commentator may be presenting it to refute it later, but within this excerpt, it is presented as a valid logical consequence if one starts from the premise of power's essential effect.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Asharite concept of kasb denies that human power has any real effect on actions.
Correction: Ibn al-Humam's argument shows that if power is given by God, it must logically produce its own effect, otherwise the distinction between voluntary and involuntary acts collapses.

Checkpoint

C) Because the slave has no power
D) Because God does not create evil

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Humam's argument reveals that if human power is real, it must have an effect, and two independent agents cannot produce one effect, leading to the conclusion that humans independently create their voluntary actions.

?
Consider a moment when you felt helpless over a sinful habit. Did you blame your circumstances or God's decree? What would it mean for you to face the reality that, according to this argument, your choices are entirely your own?

God Creates Actions but Is Not Described by Them
Refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that if God creates actions, He would be described by them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni theologians refute the Mu'tazilite claim that attributing creation of actions to God would make Him the subject of human acts, by distinguishing between the act of bringing into existence (ijad) and the inherence of the action (qiyam).

Core Idea
Creation does not imply description; only inherence does.

The Mu'tazila argued that if God creates human actions, He would be described by them, including sins. This lesson introduces the Sunni response, which distinguishes between the one who creates something and the one in whom that thing inheres. By understanding this distinction, you will see how the Ahl al-Sunna safeguard divine transcendence while affirming God's absolute creative power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the structure: it begins with the Mu'tazilite objection, then the refutation, then the scriptural response.
2
Understand the core distinction
Focus on the sentence: 'the one described by a thing is the one in whom that thing inheres, not the one who brings it into existence.' This is the key argument.
3
Apply the analogy
Consider the example of blackness: God creates blackness in a body, but He is not described as black. How does this analogy refute the objection?
4
Consider the scriptural evidence
The passage addresses verses that seem to attribute creation to humans. Notice how 'create' is reinterpreted as 'determining' or 'shaping'.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and try the activity to solidify your grasp.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قول المعتزلة : «لو كان الله خالقا لأفعال العباد لكان هو القائم والقاعد والأكل والشارب والزاني والسارق». وهذا جهل عظيم، فمدفوع بأن المتصف بالشيء من قام به ذلك الشيء لا من أوجده إذ لا يرون أن الله تعالى هو الخالق للسواد والبياض وسائر الصفات في الأجسام، فالإيجاد هو فعل الله والموجود وهو الحركة فعل العبد، وهو موصوف به حتى يشتق له منه اسم المتحرك، ولا يتصف الله بذلك، وأما قوله تعالى: فَتَبَارَكَ اللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ [المؤمنون:١٤]، بصيغة الجمع، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ تَخْلُقُ مِنَ الطِّينِ كَهَيْئَةِ الطَّيْرِ﴾ [المائدة:١١٠]، بإضافة الخلق إلى عيسى فجوابه أن الخلق هاهنا بمعنى التقدير والتصوير، فإن العبد بقدر طاقة البشرية له بعض التدبير إن وافق التقدير.
As for the Mu'tazila saying: 'If God were the creator of the actions of servants, then He would be the one standing, sitting, eating, drinking, fornicating, and stealing.' This is great ignorance. It is refuted by the fact that the one described by a thing is the one in whom that thing inheres, not the one who brings it into existence, since they do not consider that God is the creator of blackness, whiteness, and all attributes in bodies. So bringing into existence (ijad) is the act of God, and the existing thing (mawjud) which is the movement is the act of the servant, and he is described by it so that the name 'moving' is derived from it, and God is not described by that. As for His saying, 'So blessed be God, the best of creators' (23:14) in the plural form, and His saying, 'And you create from clay as the shape of a bird' (5:110) attributing creation to Jesus, the answer is that creation (khalq) here means determining (taqdir) and shaping (taswir), for the servant, within the capacity of human ability, has some management if it aligns with the predestination.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage refutes a Mu'tazilite objection. They argue that if God creates human actions, then He would be described by those actions, including sinful ones—an anthropomorphic consequence. The response distinguishes between the one who creates a thing and the one in whom the thing inheres. God creates the action, but the action inheres in the servant; thus the servant is described by it, not God. An analogy: God creates blackness in a body, but He is not described as black. Similarly, movement is created by God but inheres in the servant. The verses that use 'creator' or 'create' in reference to humans (e.g., for Jesus) are interpreted as meaning 'determining' or 'shaping,' not originating from nothing.

التصوير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates an action, He must be described by that action, because origination implies attribution.
Correction: God creates the action, but the action inheres in the creature, not in God. Description follows inherence, not origination.

Checkpoint
How does the passage refute the Mu'tazilite charge that if God creates actions, He would be described by sinful acts?

B) By distinguishing between the one who brings something into existence and the one in whom it inheres.
C) By saying that actions are not real.
D) By denying that God creates human actions.

Key Takeaway
God creates all actions, but He is not described by them because description follows inherence, not origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Mu'tazila claimed that if God creates actions, He is described by them. In your life, are there actions or thoughts you attribute to God's creation but refuse to take responsibility for? Will you accept that while God creates, the action inheres in you, and so you must answer for it?
